- 🔴 **[high/S]** The approval projection warning 'but recipe steps are NOT gated today (projection only)' (line 185–188) is rendered inline with `color: var(--warn)` in the same font size and weight as surrounding copy. This is a high-stakes honesty caveat that should be visually distinct from data rows.
  - *Fix:* Extract the caveat into a styled callout box (similar to the risk banner in RunModal): `background: color-mix(in srgb, var(--warn) 8%, transparent); border: 1px solid color-mix(in srgb, var(--warn) 30%, transparent); border-radius: var(--r-s); padding: var(--s-2) var(--s-3)` with the warning text inside. Heading: 'Approval projection (not live)' in --warn.

**Related panel (aside, page.tsx)** — Sticky right-column aside with custom inline styles (bg-1 background, line-2 border, r-2 radius); wraps RelatedPanel with groups: Recent runs (5), Connectors, Latest inbox.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The aside uses raw inline styles (lines 972–983) to build a card appearance: `background: var(--bg-1)`, `border: 1px solid var(--line-2)`, `borderRadius: var(--r-2, 8px)`. This duplicates what `PatchCard` or `GlassCard` already provides. The fallback values `var(--r-2, 8px)` and `var(--s-4, 16px)` suggest design-token uncertainty.
  - *Fix:* Replace the raw `<aside style={{...}}>` wrapper with `<PatchCard as='aside' style={{position:'sticky', top:80}}>`. This removes 8 lines of inline styles and ensures the aside stays consistent with card token updates.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The Related panel 'Recent runs' group shows up to 5 items that duplicate the 'Recent runs' PatchCard immediately to the left which shows up to 10. The operator sees the same run list in two places simultaneously.
  - *Fix:* Replace the 'Recent runs' group in RelatedPanel with a single 'All runs →' link item, or repurpose the aside group to show only items NOT visible in the main column (e.g. show only the connector health list and latest inbox; remove runs since the main card already covers them).

**Run Now modal (page.tsx RunModal)** — Dialog with recipe name in H2, optional risk banner (SimulationReport), confirmation copy or var inputs, Cancel + 'Run recipe' (btn warn) footer.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Run recipe' submit button uses `className='btn warn'` (amber/warning color). Running a recipe is a primary action, not a warning action. The warn color signals 'potentially destructive' but here it is the main CTA — the color convention is inconsistent with the action intent.
  - *Fix:* Change to `className='btn primary'` for the normal case. Reserve `btn warn` only when the simulation risk tier is 'high' — conditionally apply `className={sim?.risk.tier === 'high' ? 'btn warn' : 'btn primary'}` so the color is semantically earned.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The close button (line 237) is `<button className='btn sm ghost'>×</button>`. The `×` character is not an accessible label — screen readers will announce it as 'times' or 'multiplication sign'. `aria-label='Close'` is present, but the visible label is a mathematical symbol.
  - *Fix:* Replace `×` with the text 'Close' or an SVG X icon (16×16). If the icon-only pattern is desired, keep `aria-label='Close'` and use an SVG rather than the typographic × to avoid ambiguity.

**Not-found / error states (page.tsx)** — When recipe is not found, renders EmptyState with title 'Recipe not found'. No explicit error state for failed fetches.

- 🔴 **[high/M]** There is no error boundary or error state for when the `/api/bridge/recipes` fetch itself fails (network error, bridge offline). `useBridgeFetch` sets `recipes` to null/undefined on error; in that case `recipe` is also null but `recipes` is not a truthy array, so the not-found EmptyState never renders — the page shows the Loading skeleton indefinitely.
  - *Fix:* Expose an `error` field from `useBridgeFetch` and check `error !== null` as a distinct branch above the not-found check. Render `<ErrorState title='Could not load recipe' description={error.message} />` with a retry action. The ErrorState primitive exists.


### Recipe edit  `/recipes/[name]/edit`

**Top 3:**
1. Replace the hand-rolled AI repair dialog with the shared Dialog primitive (or at minimum add Escape-key dismissal and focus trapping) — the modal currently leaks keyboard focus to the page behind it, breaking screen-reader and keyboard-only workflows. (AI repair modal, high/M)
2. The CSS-hidden mobile sticky save bar exposes duplicate Tab stops to desktop keyboard users and the Run button inside it has no `aria-hidden` guard. Change to `aria-hidden={!isMobileViewport}` with matching `tabIndex` on children, or conditionally render based on the already-tracked `isMobileViewport` state. (Mobile sticky bar, high/S)
3. The connector preflight strip uses neutral colors even when connectors are unhealthy, making it visually indistinguishable from informational content. Escalate the card border and label to `var(--warn)` when `unhealthyConnectors.length > 0` — this is the highest-value signal on the page for preventing silent runtime failures. (Connector strip, high/S)

**Action bar (mode toggle + right-side buttons)** — Flex row with an inline-styled segmented control (YAML/Form/Flow) on the left and ghost+primary buttons on the right; everything hand-rolled with inline styles and no shared primitives.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** Mode toggle uses `aria-pressed` on individual buttons inside a `role=group`, but the segmented control pattern expects `role=radio` / `role=radiogroup` with `aria-checked`. Screen readers will announce every button as a generic toggle with no concept of mutual exclusion.
  - *Fix:* Change `role=group` to `role=radiogroup` and each button to `role=radio` with `aria-checked={editMode === mode}`. Remove `aria-pressed`.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The Save button uses dot-suffix copy ('Save •') to signal dirty state but the bullet has no accessible label — screen reader users hear 'Save bullet' and the visual signal is very low-contrast on dark theme.
  - *Fix:* Keep the dot visually but add `aria-label={dirty ? 'Save (unsaved changes)' : 'Saved'}` on the button. Optionally replace the bullet with a small badge or use the existing `dirty` className pattern seen on other pages.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The '✨ Self-correct' button only appears in YAML mode, but the mode toggle and action buttons share a single flex row. Adding/removing '✨ Self-correct' causes the right-side button group to shift layout on mode switch, which is visually jarring.
  - *Fix:* Reserve a fixed slot in the button group for the YAML-only action (e.g. min-width placeholder or always-render but hidden with `visibility:hidden`), or move it below the toolbar into the editor card footer where the 'Tab → 2 spaces · ⌘S' hint lives.

**Not-found banner** — Warn-tinted banner with 'Recipe not found' heading, inline code for the recipe name, and a ghost 'Use new-recipe form →' link. Hand-rolled div with inline styles.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** This is a structurally distinct state (creating vs editing) but uses `role=status` instead of `role=alert`. If the user lands on this URL by mistake they need immediate attention — `role=status` is polite/low-priority to AT.
  - *Fix:* Change `role=status` to `role=alert` so assistive technology announces it immediately on load.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The banner does not use the shared `EmptyState` or any shared card primitive, creating a visually inconsistent warning style vs. the shared `ErrorState` used on other pages.
  - *Fix:* Replace the hand-rolled div with `<ErrorState icon='…' title='Recipe not found' description='…' action={<Link …>}/>` or at minimum extract to a named local component so the warn/err visual language stays consistent.

**Save-error banner** — Red `role=alert` div with 'Save failed' heading, monospace error string, and an ×-dismiss button; inline styles, no shared primitive.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The dismiss × button uses `fontSize: var(--fs-xl)` and `padding: 0` giving it a 0×0 hit target far below the 44px minimum, and no visible border or focus ring on its own.
  - *Fix:* Apply `minWidth: 44px; minHeight: 44px; display: flex; align-items: center; justify-content: center` to the dismiss button, matching the min-height already used on the mode toggle buttons.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The monospace error string inside the banner is set at `var(--fs-s)` but the parent container is `var(--fs-m)`. The size inconsistency inside a single banner reads as unintentional rather than semantic.
  - *Fix:* Unify to `var(--fs-s)` for the whole banner body; reserve `var(--fs-m)` weight only for the 'Save failed' strong label.

**Lint errors banner** — Red `role=alert` banner listing all lint errors as a monospace <ul>, with an inline 'Fix with AI' button; appears above the warnings banner when both fire simultaneously.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** When both lintErrors and lintWarnings are present, the user sees two separate banners stacked with no visual grouping. The errors banner has no dismiss control, so it persists even after the user has acknowledged the errors and is actively typing a fix.
  - *Fix:* Add a dismiss button (same pattern as the save-error banner) or auto-hide the banner once lintErrors drops to zero (which the debounced lint already does). The two-banner stack rarely needs to be permanent.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** 'Fix with AI' is styled as `btn sm` (no variant class) inside an error-red banner, making it visually indistinct from the banner background on some themes. The button's purpose is high-value but easy to miss.
  - *Fix:* Change the button to `btn sm ghost` and give it a 1px border using `var(--err)` color so it pops against the red background. Add a small sparkle icon to match the `✨ Self-correct` convention.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The lint errors list renders every error with a plain integer index key (`lint-err-${idx}`) and no truncation. A recipe with 20 schema errors produces a full-height banner that pushes the editor entirely off screen.
  - *Fix:* Limit visible errors to 5 and add a 'Show all N errors' toggle. Use the error message as part of the key when available to avoid React reconciliation issues on re-lint.

**AI repair preview modal** — Fixed-position dialog with a raw `<pre>` YAML preview, optional warnings block, and Apply/Discard buttons; backdrop-click discards; hand-rolled, not using the shared Dialog primitive.

- 🔴 **[high/M]** The modal does not trap focus or set initial focus on open, so keyboard users (and screen readers) can interact with page elements behind the overlay. The shared `Dialog` primitive already implements focus trapping.
  - *Fix:* Replace the hand-rolled overlay with the shared `Dialog` component. At minimum add a `useEffect` that calls `.focus()` on the 'Apply proposal' button when `repairProposal !== null` and restores focus to the 'Fix with AI' trigger on close.
- 🔴 **[high/S]** The modal has no Escape key handler, so keyboard users cannot dismiss it without clicking 'Discard'. The backdrop-click handler only fires when `e.target === e.currentTarget`, which is correct but undiscoverable.
  - *Fix:* Add a `keydown` listener on the dialog div for `e.key === 'Escape'` that calls `discardRepair()`. If switching to the shared Dialog this comes for free.
- 🟡 **[med/M]** The `<pre>` YAML preview has `whiteSpace: pre-wrap; wordBreak: break-word` but no line numbers, making it hard to cross-reference with the editor. For long recipes the diff is invisible — the user sees a wall of YAML with no idea what changed.
  - *Fix:* Render the proposal as a read-only diff (proposed vs current) using simple line-by-line + / - coloring, or at minimum add a note like 'X lines changed'. This is a polish fix, not a feature — a simple diffLines() pass is ~20 lines.

**Lint warnings banner** — Amber `role=status` banner with a count heading and monospace <ul> of warning messages; appears below lint-errors banner and above the connector strip.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Like the lint-errors banner, there is no dismissal control and no truncation. Warnings persist even when the user intentionally keeps them (e.g. un-modeled tool refs in a known pattern).
  - *Fix:* Add a dismiss button and a 'Show N more' collapse, identical recommendation to the errors banner — implement both at once as a shared LintBanner component.

**Connector preflight strip** — Neutral surface card listing required connector chips with health dots; shows 'Connect them →' link when any connector is unhealthy.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The 'Connectors required' label is `var(--ink-2)` (faint) and `var(--fs-s)` with `fontWeight: 500`. With the neutral `var(--bg-2)` background and `var(--line-1)` border the section blends into the page — users routinely overlook the unhealthy state until the recipe fails at run time.
  - *Fix:* When `unhealthyConnectors.length > 0`, upgrade the card border to `var(--warn)` and the label to `color: var(--warn); fontWeight: 600` to match the visual urgency of the lint warning banners. Healthy state keeps the neutral styling.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Connect it/them →' link is `color: var(--info)` with no underline, making it look like faint body text rather than an actionable CTA at `var(--fs-xs)`.
  - *Fix:* Change to `className='btn sm ghost'` (link-style) so it gets the standard interactive affordance, or add `textDecoration: underline` at minimum.

**Editor card (loading / YAML / Form / Flow states)** — Single bordered card that switches between a loading div, RecipeFormView, FlowSvg, or YamlEditor based on editMode; loading state uses a bare `.empty-state` div with 'Loading…' paragraph.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The loading state inside the editor card is `<div className='empty-state'><p>Loading…</p></div>` — a plain-text fallback that ignores the shared `Skeleton`/`SkeletonList` primitives. It shows a raw unstyled paragraph for the 1–3 seconds the recipe content takes to fetch.
  - *Fix:* Replace with `<Skeleton style={{ minHeight: 400 }} />` (or a tall `SkeletonList`) to match the code-block shape and give users a perceived-performance signal matching the actual content layout.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The Flow empty state (no steps yet) uses hand-rolled faint mono text rather than the shared `EmptyState` primitive. The message 'No steps to visualize — add steps in YAML or Form view.' is useful but visually invisible at `var(--ink-3)` with no icon.
  - *Fix:* Replace the hand-rolled div with `<EmptyState icon='diagram' title='No steps yet' description='Add steps in YAML or Form view.' />`. The EmptyState icon gives the user an anchor and prevents the perception of a broken render.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The Flow SVG container has `minHeight: 300` and `overflowX: auto; overflowY: auto` but no `maxHeight` cap, meaning a large recipe can make the flow canvas expand to several thousand pixels vertically. The card itself has no scroll affordance label.
  - *Fix:* Cap `maxHeight` at `70vh` on the flow container and add `aria-label='Recipe step flow diagram'` to the scrollable div. The `overflowX: auto` is already correct for wide DAGs.

**Editor card footer / status bar (YAML mode)** — Flex row at bottom of card showing line/char count on the left and 'Linting… · Tab → 2 spaces · ⌘S to save' on the right at `var(--ink-3)` `var(--fs-xs)` — only visible in YAML mode.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The linting indicator ('Linting…') is concatenated as a string prefix to the keyboard hint, so 'Linting… · Tab → 2 spaces · ⌘S to save' reads as one run of text. When linting finishes the hint jumps leftward, creating layout shift.
  - *Fix:* Render the linting state as a separate `<span>` to the right of the hint row with an animated dot or spinner token (`aria-live='polite'`), so the keyboard shortcut hint stays stable and the linting indicator appears/disappears independently.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The ⌘S hint uses the macOS symbol exclusively. Windows/Linux users who use Ctrl+S (which IS wired in the keydown handler) see no hint that the shortcut exists.
  - *Fix:* Detect `navigator.platform` at render time and show 'Ctrl+S' on non-Mac platforms, matching the standard shortcut hint pattern.

**Deep-link step banner (inside editor card)** — Polite `role=status aria-live=polite` banner that appears when the user arrives via a `#step-<id>` hash; shows step location or not-found state; has a Dismiss button.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The 'Dismiss' button uses `border: 1px solid var(--border-default)` which is likely an undefined token (the project uses `--line-1/2/3`, not `--border-default`). This falls back to `solid black` in dark mode, creating a stark black border.
  - *Fix:* Replace `var(--border-default)` with `var(--line-2)` to match the token system used throughout this file.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The step-not-found message is shown with the same `fontWeight: 600` as the step-found message, giving both states equal visual weight. Not finding the step is a softer failure than an error but is currently presented with more emphasis than a warning.
  - *Fix:* When `!highlightLine`, display the text in `var(--ink-2)` without bold, and prefix with a small ⚠ icon. Reserve bold for the found-at-line variant.

**Mobile sticky save bar** — `.recipe-editor-mobile-savebar` div with Run and Save buttons, shown only on narrow viewports via CSS; `aria-hidden={false}` explicitly set.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The mobile Run button in the sticky bar has no `title` attribute and its label collapses to just 'Run' with no context, while the desktop Run button has a `title` warning about unsaved changes running the saved version. Mobile users get less information.
  - *Fix:* Add `title='Run the saved recipe. Unsaved changes are not included.'` to match the desktop button, and/or show an inline '(saved version)' note when `dirty === true`.
- 🔴 **[high/S]** `aria-hidden={false}` is explicitly set on the sticky bar. Since `false` is the default, this is harmless but meaningless — more importantly, when the bar is CSS-hidden on desktop the buttons remain in the tab order, causing duplicate Tab stops for desktop keyboard users.
  - *Fix:* Add `aria-hidden={!isMobileViewport}` and `tabIndex={isMobileViewport ? 0 : -1}` on the bar's children, or conditionally render the bar only when `isMobileViewport` is true (the state is already tracked in the component).


### Recipe plan  `/recipes/[name]/plan`

**Top 3:**
1. Replace the bespoke loading <p> with <SkeletonList rows={5} columns={7} /> in a role="status" aria-live container — the current raw text is the most jarring inconsistency with every other table page in the dashboard.
2. Replace the bespoke error <div> with <ErrorState title="Could not load plan" error={error} onRetry={...} /> — adds the shared icon, retry button, and proper role="alert" in one change.
3. Add role="alert" to the lint error container and normalise the prompt-cell font size to --fs-xs — the silent lint errors and the font-size jump inside the table are the two highest-friction issues for users actually reading plan output.

**Descriptor text** — A single <p> in --ink-2 at --fs-s reading "Static analysis of what this recipe will do — no execution." rendered directly inside <section> before any conditional content.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** Copy is redundant with the tab label "Plan" and the page context; it adds vertical height without conveying new information.
  - *Fix:* Replace with a shorter inline note only when lint issues exist, or move the explanation into a tooltip on a small info icon next to the tab label in the layout — removing the paragraph entirely from the page body.

**Loading state** — Raw <p> with color var(--ink-3) and font-size var(--fs-m) reading "Loading plan…" — no skeleton, no animation, no aria role.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The bespoke loading paragraph bypasses the shared Skeleton primitives (SkeletonList, SkeletonRow) that every other list/table page uses, creating an inconsistent loading experience.
  - *Fix:* Replace with <SkeletonList rows={5} columns={7} /> wrapped in a <div role="status" aria-live="polite" aria-label="Loading plan"> to match the pattern in Runs, Traces, and Approvals pages.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** No aria-live announcement means screen-reader users get no feedback that the plan is loading.
  - *Fix:* Add role="status" aria-live="polite" to the loading container regardless of which skeleton approach is chosen.

**Error state** — Bespoke <div> with inline styles (err-soft background, err border, err color) rendering the error string — no icon, no retry affordance, no shared ErrorState component.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The inline error block ignores the shared <ErrorState> primitive that has a centered icon, title/description separation, monospace detail block, and optional retry button — inconsistent with every other page's error presentation.
  - *Fix:* Replace the inline <div> with <ErrorState title="Could not load plan" error={error} onRetry={() => void load()} /> from @/components/patchwork/ErrorState. Expose the load function via useCallback so onRetry can re-trigger it.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Error state has no retry mechanism; a transient bridge timeout leaves the user stranded with no way to recover without a full page reload.
  - *Fix:* Add onRetry callback to trigger re-fetch (pairs with the ErrorState fix above).

**Meta row (plan summary bar)** — A flex-wrap pill bar inside a bg-2 / line-1 rounded box showing Trigger, Steps, Est. tokens, Min. cost, Has write steps warning, Connectors, and Generated time — all inline with <strong> highlights.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** "Est. tokens" and "Min. cost" tooltips contain dense caveats (output tokens not counted, cache effects not modelled) in title attributes — invisible on touch devices and never read by screen readers.
  - *Fix:* Surface a short asterisk footnote below the meta row (e.g., "* Input-only estimate @ Sonnet pricing. Actual cost will be higher.") rather than hiding explanation in title. Remove the title attributes.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** "Generated {time}" at marginLeft:auto is right-aligned within the flex-wrap row, but on narrow viewports the row wraps and the timestamp lands inline with other items instead of at far right, breaking the intended visual separation.
  - *Fix:* Move the generated timestamp to a separate row below the meta bar (or use a full-width separator line) so it does not rely on marginLeft:auto within a flex-wrap context.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The warning "⚠ Has write steps" uses a raw Unicode character for the icon, which can render inconsistently across fonts and OSes and has no aria-label, so screen readers announce the literal glyph name.
  - *Fix:* Replace the ⚠ character with an inline SVG icon (matching the warn icon used in StatusPill/ErrorState) and add aria-label="Warning" or wrap in a <span role="img" aria-label="Warning">.

**Lint messages section** — Conditional block rendering per-error and per-warning <div> banners with bespoke inline styles (err-soft/err and warn-tinted/warn borders) and ✕/⚠ Unicode prefixes — no grouping label, no icon component, no role.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** Each lint item is an unstyled <div> with no role="alert" or aria-live region; errors appear silently to assistive technology.
  - *Fix:* Add role="alert" to the error container and role="status" to the warning container so the content is announced on appearance.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The lint section has no section heading, making it hard to scan when there are multiple items mixed with the meta row above and the steps table below.
  - *Fix:* Add a small <h3> label ("Lint issues") above the lint items, styled like the "Parallel groups" heading already in the page (--ink-2, --fs-s, fontWeight 600) — costs nothing and anchors the block visually.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** ✕ and ⚠ are raw Unicode; they render with variable glyph weight and do not inherit color reliably in all browsers.
  - *Fix:* Use inline SVGs matching the icon set already used in ErrorState (circle-X for errors, triangle-warn for warnings).

**Steps table** — A 7-column <table> (# / ID / Type / Tool-or-prompt / Output / Risk / Flags) with a bg-2 thead, line-1 row dividers, per-cell inline padding, and conditional err-tinted row background for unresolved steps.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The "Tool / prompt" column (maxWidth 360) renders prompt text at --fs-s while all other cells are --fs-xs, creating a noticeable size jump that breaks table rhythm, especially as the two-line clamp can make rows taller than their neighbors.
  - *Fix:* Normalise prompt text to --fs-xs (matching the rest of the table). Two-line clamp is fine to keep; just remove the fontSize override on the prompt <span> at line 438.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The table has no aria-label or <caption>, so screen readers announce it as a generic table with no context.
  - *Fix:* Add <caption style={{display:'none'}}>Recipe execution plan steps</caption> as the first child of <table>, or add aria-label="Recipe execution plan steps" to the <table> element.
- ⚪ **[low/M]** Column "#" is a bare ordinal and column "ID" is the step's machine ID; both are faint/mono but their purpose distinction is not obvious without reading column headers. On narrow viewports (overflowX: auto) the table scrolls horizontally with no sticky first column, so context is lost.
  - *Fix:* Make the "#" + "ID" columns sticky (position: sticky; left: 0; background: inherit) so they remain visible during horizontal scroll on small screens.

**Parallel groups section** — Conditional section rendered only when plan.parallelGroups is non-empty; shows a flex-wrap row of mono-font pill chips, each displaying [stepId, stepId, …] notation with an <h3> heading.

- 🟡 **[med/M]** Parallel group chips are purely informational but visually identical to the step ID cells in the table above — there is no visual link between a group chip and the corresponding table rows it references, forcing users to manually cross-reference.
  - *Fix:* Add a hover/focus highlight on each group chip that applies a CSS class (e.g., .step-highlighted) to matching <tr> elements in the steps table via a client-side hover handler, so users can see which rows belong to each group without manual lookup.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The section title "Parallel groups" is rendered in --ink-2 at --fs-s, which is lighter and smaller than the table header cells (--ink-2, --fs-xs at the th level) but displayed as an <h3>. The hierarchy feels inverted — the heading looks softer than the data.
  - *Fix:* Promote to --ink-1 or --ink-0 at --fs-m for the heading to give it proper visual weight, distinguishing it clearly from the chip labels below.

**Empty state (no steps)** — No empty state branch exists — when plan.steps is an empty array the steps table renders with a thead and an empty tbody, showing a table with headers and no rows.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** An empty steps array produces a visually broken table (headers with no body rows) with no user-facing explanation. A recipe might have zero steps during scaffold or after all steps are removed.
  - *Fix:* Add a zero-steps guard: when plan.steps.length === 0 render <EmptyState title="No steps" description="This recipe has no steps defined yet." /> from @/components/patchwork/EmptyState instead of the table.


### Recipe new (create)  `/recipes/new`

**Top 3:**
1. Add aria-expanded + aria-controls to the AI generation panel toggle button — currently the collapsible has no accessibility state announcement for screen readers.
2. Apply .btn.primary to the 'Create YAML draft' submit button — the primary creation action is visually indistinguishable from secondary controls, undermining hierarchy on the page's most important interaction.
3. Add an inline slug preview below the Name input showing the normalized form (e.g. 'Will be saved as: my-daily-report.yaml') — without it, users typing natural-language names have no feedback until they see the YAML preview panel, which is hidden off-screen on mobile.

**Page header** — h1 'New recipe' with a .page-head-sub subtitle explaining the form→YAML→editor flow; no breadcrumb or back link to /recipes.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** No breadcrumb or back-nav. The Cancel button is buried far below in the actions row, so users who land here by accident have no immediate escape route visible at the top.
  - *Fix:* Add a small back-link or breadcrumb row above .page-head (e.g. '← Recipes') using the existing --ink-2 / --fs-s treatment already used on detail pages. The Cancel button below can stay for confirmation symmetry.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The .page-head-sub subtitle is a full two-sentence explanation ('Start with structured fields, save a YAML recipe draft, then continue in the source editor.') that duplicates intent already conveyed by the scope banner immediately below. Reading load is doubled.
  - *Fix:* Shorten to a single clause: 'Scaffolds a YAML draft — continue in the source editor after saving.' Removes the redundancy with the scope banner.

**Scope / capability banner** — role='note' div with --bg-2 background and --border-subtle border explaining the form does not cover tool: steps, parallel: groups, or file-watch/git-hook triggers.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The banner uses raw inline styles (background, border, borderRadius, padding) rather than the existing .pill.info or the shared alert/callout pattern. It will diverge visually from other info callouts when design tokens are updated.
  - *Fix:* Replace the bespoke inline style block with a class that composes the existing .pill.info or .alert-info treatment — at minimum extract to a .recipe-scope-note utility class in globals.css so the token path is centralized.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The banner uses var(--border-subtle) but the token is aliased to --line-1 which is the faintest border; the enclosing AI panel uses var(--border-default) (--line-2). The inconsistency makes the scope note look less prominent than the AI section even though it is higher-priority information.
  - *Fix:* Switch the scope banner border to var(--border-default) to match the visual weight of the surrounding sections.

**AI generation panel (collapsible)** — Collapsible section with a toggle button, AutoGrowTextarea prompt input, Generate button, and (when result arrives) a syntax-highlighted pre block with 'Save and edit' / 'Discard' actions.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The toggle button lacks aria-expanded, so screen readers cannot announce the open/closed state. The panel content also lacks an id for aria-controls.
  - *Fix:* Add aria-expanded={aiOpen} to the toggle button and aria-controls='ai-panel' to pair it with id='ai-panel' on the collapsible div. This is a one-line change per attribute.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'NEW' badge uses var(--info) (blue) as a background with hardcoded color: '#fff'. In light ('paper') theme, --info resolves to a medium blue where white text is ~4.5:1 — borderline AA. More importantly, 'NEW' adds no functional information for returning users and creates persistent visual noise.
  - *Fix:* Remove the 'NEW' badge entirely, or gate it behind a flag that clears after first use (e.g. localStorage). If kept, switch to .pill.info so it inherits the audited contrast treatment.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The AI YAML result pre block has no syntax highlighting applied — it renders raw YAML as plain --ink-0 text — while the form-side YAML preview uses highlightYaml(). The inconsistency makes the AI result harder to scan.
  - *Fix:* Wrap the aiResult.yaml rendering in highlightYaml() (already imported on line 6), same as the preview pre at line 1648.

**Form — Name and Description fields** — Standard label+input layout; Name uses font-mono, Description uses AutoGrowTextarea with font-sans; both have --bg-2 background with --border-default.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** Name input uses fontFamily: var(--font-mono) which is appropriate for the slug but the label gives no hint that the value will be slugified. A user who types 'My Daily Report' will see the slug differ from their input only in the YAML preview — there is no inline slug preview next to the field.
  - *Fix:* Below the Name input (before any error), add a one-line slug preview: 'Will be saved as: my-daily-report.yaml' in --fs-xs / --ink-3. This can reuse the safeName computed value already on line 527.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The name validation error message ('Name must produce a slug starting with a letter or digit and containing only letters, digits, or hyphens (max 64 chars).') is 94 characters — the longest error text on the page. It describes the constraint on the output slug, not what the user typed wrong.
  - *Fix:* Shorten to: 'Becomes slug — use letters, digits, spaces, or hyphens only (max 64 chars).' Lead with what they can type, not the internal slug rule.

**Form — Trigger section** — Select dropdown for trigger type (Manual/Webhook/Schedule) with conditional sub-inputs for webhook path (prefix+input compound) and cron expression.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The cron input (placeholder '0 9 * * 1-5') has no helper text explaining the field order (minute hour day month weekday), no link to a cron reference, and validation only fires on submit. Users unfamiliar with cron syntax will guess or leave it blank.
  - *Fix:* Add a single hint line below the cron input in --fs-xs / --ink-3: 'minute hour day month weekday — e.g. 0 9 * * 1-5 = weekdays at 9am'. No external link needed; the example in the placeholder already exists and just needs context.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** When trigger type is 'manual', there is no supporting copy explaining how a manual recipe is actually triggered (e.g. via the dashboard Run button, CLI recipe run, or API). The select gives three options but only two show contextual help.
  - *Fix:* Add a single hint sentence for the manual case: 'Run from the dashboard, CLI (patchwork recipe run <name>), or API.' Same --fs-xs / --ink-3 treatment as cron hint.

**Form — Variables section** — Optional section with '+ Add variable' button; empty state shows a faint --ink-3 hint; each var renders as a .new-recipe-var-card with name / description / required / default fields.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Required' checkbox inside each var card has no associated htmlFor/id pair — the label wraps the input natively which is valid, but the visible 'Required' text is at --ink-2 / --fs-s making it easy to miss. The checkbox itself has no visible focus ring beyond the browser default.
  - *Fix:* Give the checkbox input id='var-required-{i}' and the label htmlFor='var-required-{i}'. Add a focus-visible style in .new-recipe-var-card that matches the orange accent ring already defined for .new-recipe-field-input:focus.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The 'Default value' input is --fs-s while Name and Description inputs are --fs-m, creating inconsistent type scale within the same card. The size difference implies hierarchy that does not match the actual field importance.
  - *Fix:* Unify all three row-level inputs (name, description, default) to --fs-m. The 'Default value' can remain visually secondary through its placeholder text alone.

**Form — Steps section** — One step pre-populated; each .new-recipe-step-card has a header row with label + move-up/move-down/remove buttons and a full-width textarea for the agent prompt.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Move-up/move-down buttons (▲ ▼ HTML entities) have no visible label and their disabled state relies only on the HTML disabled attribute — the button opacity is not suppressed by a CSS :disabled rule in .btn.ghost, so disabled move buttons look identical to enabled ones until the user tries to click.
  - *Fix:* Add opacity: 0.38; cursor: not-allowed; to .btn.ghost:disabled (or .btn.sm.ghost:disabled) in globals.css. The aria-labels are already correct; this is purely a visual fix.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The step prompt textarea uses resize: vertical which allows the user to drag the height but the page also imports AutoGrowTextarea for other fields. The step textarea does not use AutoGrowTextarea, so it starts at 3 rows and requires manual drag — inconsistent with description and AI prompt fields.
  - *Fix:* Replace the bare textarea with AutoGrowTextarea (already imported) and set maxHeight={320}. Remove resize: vertical from the inline style. Consistent auto-grow across all multi-line inputs.

**Form actions bar (submit / cancel)** — Inline flex row with 'Create YAML draft' (.btn default) and 'Cancel' (.btn.ghost) buttons; submitError renders .alert-err above; submitNotice renders an ad-hoc role='status' div.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The primary submit button uses the default .btn style (surface background, --ink-1 text) rather than .btn.primary (orange fill). On a creation page the primary action should be visually dominant. Other creation flows in the dashboard use .btn.primary for this slot.
  - *Fix:* Add className='btn primary' to the submit button (line 1587) instead of just 'btn'. No layout change needed.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The submitNotice (demo-mode warning) is a bespoke role='status' div with plain --ink-1 text and --border-default border — visually indistinguishable from an info note. Demo mode is a meaningful constraint and should register as a warning.
  - *Fix:* Replace the bespoke div with .pill.warn or the existing alert warn pattern so the border and text color use --warn, matching how other demo-mode notices are surfaced.

**YAML preview panel** — Right-column (>900px) or bottom-stacked (<900px) pre block with highlightYaml() output, a 'YAML preview' label, and a CopyYamlButton; a hint line notes saving creates a .yaml file.

- 🟡 **[med/M]** Below 900px the YAML preview stacks below the entire form — after Steps, Variables, and Actions. On a typical phone this means the preview is ~1500px below the fold. Users who want to validate the YAML while typing have no feedback until they scroll past all form sections.
  - *Fix:* On mobile, move the YAML preview above the submit actions (between Steps and the actions row) rather than at the very bottom. Alternatively collapse it behind a 'Preview YAML' disclosure button on mobile so it is accessible without the scroll penalty.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The 'YAML preview' label is --fs-s / --ink-2 / fontWeight 500, which gives it less visual weight than the section labels in the form ('Name', 'Steps', etc.) at --fs-m / --ink-1 / fontWeight 500. The preview panel has no clear visual boundary separating it from the form column.
  - *Fix:* Elevate the YAML preview header to --fs-m / --ink-1, matching the form section label treatment. On desktop, add a subtle left border (1px solid var(--border-subtle)) to visually separate the two columns.

**Suspense / loading state** — Suspense fallback is a bare div.empty-state with role='status' aria-live='polite' containing the text 'Loading recipe editor…'.

- ⚪ **[low/M]** The fallback uses .empty-state class but renders only a plain text paragraph — it does not use the shared Skeleton primitive (SkeletonList or a custom skeleton matching the form layout). The jump from text placeholder to full form is jarring.
  - *Fix:* Replace the text fallback with a skeleton that roughly mirrors the form shape: two SkeletonStatCard or Skeleton rows for Name/Description, one for Trigger, one for Steps. Even three Skeleton bars avoids the layout shift.


### Recipe compare  `/recipes/compare`

**Top 3:**
1. Replace the missing-nameB empty state with an in-page recipe selector input — currently the user must manually edit the URL to provide ?b=, which is the primary entry workflow and is completely undiscoverable.
2. Fill removed-step rows with the actual step data (tool name, risk, mode) by building a merged stepById map from both plans — currently removed rows show only a red dot and blank cells, defeating the purpose of the diff.
3. Replace per-column error divs with the shared ErrorState primitive and add a retry callback — currently fetch failures leave the column permanently broken with no recovery path short of a full page reload.

**Page header** — BackLink + h1 'Compare variants' + .page-head-sub subtitle string; no recipe names or trigger-type context visible in the header itself.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** Subtitle buries the signal — 'Dry-run plan diff — green rows are steps unique to this variant, red rows are removed. Promote to replace the base recipe.' is 20+ words that duplicate the legend below.
  - *Fix:* Trim .page-head-sub to 'Side-by-side dry-run plan diff. Promote a variant to replace the base recipe.' — 12 words. The legend already explains row colors.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** h1 says 'Compare variants' but shows no recipe names — user loses orientation after scrolling or landing directly from a deep link.
  - *Fix:* Append the base recipe name to the h1 or add a subtitle: 'Comparing variants of <code>{baseName}</code>' rendered beneath the h1 using the already-computed baseName variable.

**Suspense fallback / page-level loading state** — Outer Suspense renders a bare <p style={{ color: 'var(--ink-2)' }}>Loading…</p> with no structure or skeleton.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Plain 'Loading…' paragraph has no layout — page shifts dramatically when CompareInner mounts, causing layout jank.
  - *Fix:* Replace with a two-column skeleton that mirrors the compare-columns layout: two .compare-panel shaped divs each containing 3 SkeletonList rows (or the custom compareSkelPulse divs already in PlanColumn's loading branch). This fallback is only for the SSR/Suspense boundary; the per-column loading state is already handled.

**Empty / missing-params state** — Raw <div className='empty-state'> with inline JSX — partially duplicates the EmptyState primitive; includes a <Link> styled as .btn.sm.primary for back-navigation.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** Manually assembles empty-state markup instead of using the EmptyState component, which already handles the dashed-border card, centered layout, icon slot, and action slot.
  - *Fix:* Replace with <EmptyState title={...} description={...} action={<Link href='/recipes' className='btn sm primary'>← Back to recipes</Link>} /> — one import, no custom JSX.
- 🔴 **[high/M]** When nameA is present but nameB is missing, the copy tells the user to add ?b= manually. This is not discoverable — there is no input or selector to pick the second recipe.
  - *Fix:* Add a small recipe-name text input (or a link to /recipes with instructions to use the Compare button) so the user can fill the missing slot without editing the URL bar. Even a plain <input type='text' placeholder='recipe-name-v2'> that updates the URL via router.push would unblock the core workflow.

**Diff legend** — .compare-legend strip with two dot + label items at --fs-xs color --ink-3; rendered between the header and the columns; uses custom .compare-legend-dot divs.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Legend text is --ink-3 (faintest token) at --fs-xs — likely fails AA contrast on both light and dark themes when rendered against the page canvas.
  - *Fix:* Bump to --ink-2 to match .page-head-sub contrast level. No sizing change needed.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** Legend is always visible even when both columns are still loading, which is confusing — it describes row colors before any rows exist.
  - *Fix:* Conditionally render the legend only when at least one plan has loaded: {(planA || planB) && <div className='compare-legend'>…</div>}.

**Column header (PlanColumn header bar)** — Dark bg-2 bar with <code> recipe name, step count pill, +N/−N diff pills, and a Promote button; uses inline styles for bg/border/padding.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Promote button label 'Promote → {targetName}' truncates on narrow screens because the column is flex:1 with min-width:0 — the button text overflows or wraps awkwardly when recipe names are long.
  - *Fix:* Set a max-width on the <code> name and add text-overflow: ellipsis; overflow: hidden; white-space: nowrap, or shorten the button label to 'Promote' and rely on the existing title attribute for full context.
- ⚪ **[low/M]** Column header uses bg-2 + border-default via inline style — not using PatchCard or GlassCard, so it won't pick up any card-hover or theme token updates made to those primitives.
  - *Fix:* Wrap PlanColumn in <PatchCard> instead of a raw <div> with manual border/radius/overflow. Move the header content into PatchCard's header slot if it supports one, otherwise keep the internal structure and just swap the outer wrapper.

**Per-column loading state (skeleton)** — Three hard-coded height:32 divs with inline background, opacity, and animation — custom compareSkelPulse keyframe defined in globals.css.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** Custom skeleton divs duplicate the Skeleton/SkeletonList primitives available in the codebase; when the shared skeleton style changes, this column won't update.
  - *Fix:* Replace the three custom divs with <SkeletonList count={3} /> (or the equivalent Skeleton primitive) — consistent pulse animation, no custom keyframe needed.

**Per-column error state** — Inline <div className='alert-err' style={{ fontSize: 'var(--fs-s)' }}>{error}</div> — shows raw error string with no retry affordance.

- 🔴 **[high/M]** Error state is a bare alert-err div with no retry button. If the plan API is transiently unavailable, the user has no recovery path without reloading the page.
  - *Fix:* Replace with <ErrorState error={error} onRetry={() => void refetch()} /> using the shared ErrorState primitive. Add a refetch callback that re-runs the useEffect fetch for the relevant column.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** alert-err has font-size: var(--fs-s) override that conflicts with the base .alert-err rule (font-size 13px / --fs-m equivalent). Overriding makes the error text smaller than the component's own design intent.
  - *Fix:* Remove the inline fontSize override and rely on the .alert-err rule.

**Lint warnings / errors banners** — alert-err div for lint.errors and a hand-rolled yellow div for lint.warnings — both join multiple messages with ' · ' separator.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The warnings block uses full inline styles (background, border, borderRadius, padding, fontSize, color) rather than any shared alert-warn or similar token. It will diverge from any future warning-alert design updates.
  - *Fix:* Add a .alert-warn class to globals.css mirroring .alert-err but with --warn colors, and use <div className='alert-warn'> here. Alternatively reuse the same color-mix pattern but with a named class.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Multiple lint messages joined with ' · ' is unreadable when there are 3+ messages — they form an unpunctuated run-on sentence.
  - *Fix:* Render each lint error/warning as a separate <p> or <li> inside the alert, or join with ' • ' and add aria-label='Lint errors' on the container for screen readers.

**Steps table (StepRow)** — Four-column <table> with Step (mono font), Risk pill, Mode (read/write), and an unresolved badge; diff rows use color-mix backgrounds and colored dots; risk uses raw .pill class with RISK_PILL mapping.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Risk column uses a hand-rolled <span className={`pill ${RISK_PILL[step.risk]}`}> mapping — the RiskPill primitive already exists in patchwork/ and includes an aria-label plus the colored dot. The custom mapping duplicates logic and misses the aria-label.
  - *Fix:* Replace <span className={`pill ${RISK_PILL[step.risk]}`}>{step.risk}</span> with <RiskPill level={step.risk} /> imported from @/components/patchwork.
- 🔴 **[high/M]** Removed-step rows pass step={{ id, type: 'agent' }} as a stub — the tool name, risk, and mode columns are all empty, making the removed row show only a red dot and blank cells. The user cannot tell what was removed.
  - *Fix:* Pass the full removed step object by maintaining a merged step map (stepById) built from both plans before rendering, then look up the removed step's tool/risk/isWrite from that map when rendering a removed row.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Colored backgrounds alone distinguish new vs removed steps (WCAG 1.4.1 — color cannot be the sole differentiator). The aria-label on the colored dot helps screen readers but sighted users with color blindness cannot distinguish the two states.
  - *Fix:* Add a text label column or prefix: '+ NEW' / '− REMOVED' in a small muted pill next to the step name, in addition to the color dot.

**Connectors footer (per-column)** — Plain <p> listing connector namespaces as a comma-joined string at --fs-xs --ink-2 below the steps table; no chip or structured display.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** Connector namespaces rendered as raw comma-separated text — ConnectorChip or KeyChip primitives exist for exactly this purpose and provide consistent visual treatment.
  - *Fix:* Replace the <p> with a flex row of <ConnectorChip namespace={ns} /> (or <KeyChip label={ns} />) for each namespace in plan.connectorNamespaces.

**Promote result banner** — Inline div with role='alert'/'status', color-mix backgrounds, and a 'Back to recipes' link — appears above the columns after a promote action; uses promoteResultIn animation.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Success banner persists indefinitely — no auto-dismiss or close button. After a successful promote the user is likely done; the banner competes with the columns for attention.
  - *Fix:* Add an auto-dismiss (5s setTimeout → setPromoteResult(null)) and/or an × close button. On success, the 'Back to recipes →' link is already provided, so auto-dismiss is safe.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The ✓ checkmark is rendered as a Unicode character inside aria-hidden='true' span — screen readers will still announce the surrounding text without any explicit 'Success' prefix.
  - *Fix:* Prepend an explicit accessible label: 'Promoted successfully: ' as visually hidden text when promoteResultKind === 'ok', and 'Error: ' when 'err', before the message string.

**Confirm overwrite Dialog** — Uses shared Dialog component; Cancel and Overwrite buttons are hand-rolled with inline padding/border/background/cursor styles rather than .btn classes.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Dialog action buttons use raw inline styles instead of .btn classes — no focus-visible ring, no disabled state, and they will not pick up .btn hover/active transitions or theme updates.
  - *Fix:* Replace inline-styled buttons with <button className='btn sm secondary'> for Cancel and <button className='btn sm destructive'> (or the closest danger variant) for Overwrite.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** Dialog body repeats <code>{baseName}</code> twice in adjacent sentences — 'Overwrite {baseName}?' heading then '{baseName} already exists.' — redundant.
  - *Fix:* Remove the second occurrence: 'This recipe already exists. Promoting {variantName} will replace it. The existing file will be overwritten.'

**Responsive / mobile layout** — compare-columns stacks to single column below 768px via flex-wrap. Column header has fixed-layout flex row with Promote button that may overflow on narrow viewports.

- 🟡 **[med/M]** On mobile both columns stack vertically, so the user must scroll to compare them — the diff relationship is lost. There is no summary of differences at the page level to compensate.
  - *Fix:* Add a summary diff row above the columns (visible on all breakpoints, but especially useful on mobile) showing total added / removed / common steps across both variants: e.g. 'A: 5 steps (+2 new, −1 removed) vs B: 4 steps'.


### Marketplace  `/marketplace`

**Top 3:**
1. Move TrustMetadataCard and TrustDivergenceNotice above the YAML preview on the recipe detail page — the trust divergence notice is the most safety-critical signal on the page and is currently buried below potentially hundreds of lines of YAML, after the install button the user has already clicked.
2. Fix the 'Featured this week' section: it unconditionally promotes the first registry array entry with an editorial label, uses a broken --card-bg token that likely renders as transparent, and the orange glow disappears entirely in light/paper theme — undermining both trust and visual consistency.
3. The submit form's recipe-submit-layout class is intended to produce a 2-column desktop layout (metadata left, YAML editor right) but the inline style sets gridTemplateColumns to '1fr', meaning the two-column grid only works if the CSS class overrides it; if the class is missing or mis-scoped the form is a single stacked column on all viewports. Verify and fix the grid so metadata and YAML sit side-by-side on desktop as the comments describe.

**Status banner (bridge offline / unauth)** — Full-width purple-soft band with inline CTA link; rendered before the page heading; uses raw inline styles with --purple / --purple-soft tokens rather than a shared component.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Uses ad-hoc inline styles (--purple-soft background, --purple border, --accent-soft CTA pill) that don't match the semantic token set used elsewhere (--warn-soft / --ok-soft / --err-soft). The result is an inconsistent purple-tinted strip that reads as decorative rather than actionable.
  - *Fix:* Replace the bespoke div with the existing HintCard or an alert-style primitive. If the pattern must stay custom, switch to --info-soft/--info token pair (or --warn-soft for the offline case) to align with the rest of the dashboard's alert language.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Browsing in preview mode' copy for the offline state is vague — 'preview mode' is not a defined concept anywhere on the page, and users who have the bridge installed but offline won't know what 'preview' means.
  - *Fix:* Change to: 'Bridge not connected — install recipes via the CLI or start the bridge first.' Remove the word 'preview mode' entirely.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The banner is hidden during bridgeStatus==='checking' to avoid a flash, but there is no loading indicator at all during that window (typically 0–4 s on 3G). Users with a slow bridge connection see nothing at the top of the page while the CTA buttons are also hidden (the card renders an invisible spacer).
  - *Fix:* Add a small shimmer or a 1-line 'Checking bridge…' faint-text placeholder during the checking state so the page doesn't appear broken.

**Page header (title + subtitle + Search/Submit controls)** — editorial-h1 with accent span tagline, editorial-sub with recipe count + source URL, plus Search toggle and Submit CTA in a flex row.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The editorial tagline 'open-source YAML, curated.' is decorative copy buried inside the h1 element. On small screens the h1 wraps awkwardly because the span is inline inside the heading, and the tagline competes visually with the recipe count subtitle rather than reinforcing a hierarchy.
  - *Fix:* Move the tagline out of the h1 into the editorial-sub line (or drop it). The h1 should read just 'Marketplace'. The subtitle already supplies the essential signal ('9 recipes · sourced from …').
- 🟡 **[med/M]** 'Search' is a toggle button that reveals a hidden input rather than an always-visible search box. On desktop there is ample room in the page-head action row; hiding it behind a click adds a step with no space benefit and no keyboard shortcut.
  - *Fix:* Show the search input inline in the page-head row (max-width ~260 px) on viewports ≥ 768 px. Keep the toggle-only pattern on mobile. This eliminates the reveal click for the common case.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** 'Submit a recipe' CTA lives in the header but competes equally with 'Search'; no visual hierarchy separates a primary exploration action (Search) from a secondary contribution action (Submit).
  - *Fix:* Demote 'Submit a recipe' to a ghost/secondary btn and keep Search as the primary action, or move Submit to the page footer area. Currently both are btn sm, but Submit is styled primary — this makes Submit appear more important than Search.

**Fallback / load-error notice** — Single alert-err div rendered below the header when both bridge and GitHub registry are unreachable; shows the fallback snapshot date inline.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The alert-err class is the same red error styling used for hard failures elsewhere (e.g. lint errors in the Submit page). A stale-cache banner is a degraded-state warning, not a hard error. The colour and urgency level are misleading.
  - *Fix:* Switch to the warn styling class (or inline --warn-soft/--warn tokens matching the pattern used in RegistryUnreachable) and prefix with 'Note:' rather than leaving it as a bare error-coloured block.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The message 'registry unreachable — showing built-in fallback (snapshot 2026-05-23)' starts with a technical identifier; the user's first question is 'what can I do?', not when the snapshot was taken.
  - *Fix:* Rewrite as: 'Couldn't reach the live registry — showing a built-in snapshot from 2026-05-23. Refresh to retry.' Lead with action, end with context.

**Loading skeleton grid** — Six glass-card skeletons in marketplace-grid with Skeleton + SkeletonText primitives; no section label during loading; grid is aria-busy=true.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The skeleton grid has no visible section label (no 'Loading recipes…' heading or sr-only text that screen readers would announce beyond the aria-label on the grid container). Sighted users who land mid-load see six empty cards with no signal about what they're waiting for.
  - *Fix:* Add an sr-only or visually present caption ('Loading marketplace…') above the skeleton grid, consistent with how other pages handle loading states (or use SkeletonList if a list-form skeleton is more appropriate here).
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The skeleton cards include a Skeleton icon placeholder (20×20) that doesn't appear in the real RecipeCard (which has no icon). The skeleton mis-shapes the card's visual weight during load, causing a layout shift when real cards appear.
  - *Fix:* Remove the icon Skeleton (the first row in the skeleton card). Match the skeleton structure to the real card: title-width SkeletonText, two body SkeletonTexts, then pill-width Skeletons.

**Featured recipe section** — First registry item displayed in a full-width orange-bordered wrapper with a '★ Featured' absolute-positioned pill; always the index-0 recipe regardless of any featured flag in the registry.

- 🔴 **[high/M]** 'Featured this week' implies editorial curation, but the featured item is always the first entry in the registry array (filtered[0]). If the registry order changes or a user searches (search hides the featured section entirely), the label is misleading.
  - *Fix:* Either rename to 'Highlighted' / 'First recipe' to be honest about the static ordering, or add a featured:true flag to RegistryRecipe and only render this section when such a recipe exists. The current heuristic breaks trust if a low-quality recipe happens to be first.
- 🔴 **[high/S]** The featured wrapper uses color-mix(in srgb, var(--accent) 16%, var(--card-bg)) for its background, but --card-bg is not defined in the token list (the system uses --surface / --bg-1 / --bg-2). This likely falls back to transparent, producing an unstyled orange-outline box on some themes.
  - *Fix:* Replace --card-bg with var(--surface) or var(--bg-2). Verify in both paper and dark themes.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The orange 'glow' box-shadow (0 1px 14px color-mix(in srgb, var(--accent) 20%, transparent)) is effective in dark mode but disappears entirely on the paper/light theme where the canvas is near-white. The featured card is visually indistinguishable from a regular card in light mode.
  - *Fix:* Increase the shadow opacity to 35% for light theme via a data-theme selector or use a subtle dashed --accent border with a higher-contrast background tint. Alternatively, make the '★ Featured' pill more visually prominent (larger, branded colour) to carry the distinction without relying on the shadow.

**Recipe card grid** — CSS grid (.marketplace-grid) with RecipeCard components; each card has name link, maintainer, description (3-line clamp), trust badges, connector dots, download count, and Install/Installed/Get Patchwork CTA.

- 🟡 **[med/M]** Connector dots are colored circles showing 2-character initials (e.g. 'SL' for Slack, 'GM' for Gmail). They have title and aria-label attributes, but the initials themselves are hard to parse at the dot's small size and there is no legend. Users unfamiliar with the color coding cannot identify connectors without hovering.
  - *Fix:* Replace or supplement the colored initials dot with a compact text pill (matching the BundleCard's connector pill pattern) or at minimum increase dot size to 24×24 and use 1-letter initials. Add a visually accessible legend tooltip on the connector row or use ConnectorChip if available.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The download count (↓ N) is only rendered when downloads > 0, but all fallback registry items have downloads: 0. The metric never appears, making the count field dead code in practice. More importantly, showing zeros would be useful social proof (or a signal to distrust the data) — the current conditional silently hides the absence.
  - *Fix:* Either remove the downloads field from the card layout entirely until live data is available, or show '↓ —' / 'New' for zero-count recipes so the absence is explicit rather than invisible.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The inline error div on the card (shown when an install fails) has no max-height or truncation. A long error message (e.g. the not_allowlisted mapped message, which is 95 chars) pushes the card footer down and can misalign the grid row. There is also no dismiss button.
  - *Fix:* Clamp the error text to 2 lines with text-overflow or a details/summary disclosure. Add a small dismiss (×) button or auto-clear after 8 s (matching the Toast pattern).

**Bundle card grid** — BundleCard renders as a full Link wrapper (glass-card) with mono bundle name, 'bundle' info pill, description, connector pills (max 4 + overflow), and recipe/plugin/policy metadata row.

- 🟡 **[med/M]** BundleCard's connector items render as plain .pill text chips (e.g. 'slack', 'linear') while RecipeCard renders colored initials dots. This inconsistency across two card types on the same page means connector identity is communicated differently depending on whether you're looking at a recipe or a bundle.
  - *Fix:* Standardise connector display: use the same colored dot or pill pattern in both card types. If the dot is kept for recipes, reuse it here; if the pill is preferred, migrate recipes to pills.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The bundle name is rendered in var(--font-mono) with var(--accent) color and whitespace:nowrap + textOverflow:ellipsis. On narrow viewports (< 320 px) or for long bundle names, the mono name silently truncates with no tooltip revealing the full name. The overflow is only visible on hover in browsers that show title attributes.
  - *Fix:* Add a title attribute with the full bundle name (bundle.name) on the name span, or allow the name to wrap to two lines (remove whitespace:nowrap and set overflow:hidden with a 2-line clamp instead).
- ⚪ **[low/S]** There is no empty state for the bundles section — if bundles.length > 0 then the section renders, but if the fetch returns bundles: [] only recipes show with no indication that bundles exist or whether the section failed to load.
  - *Fix:* This is acceptable (section is conditionally rendered) but add a loading skeleton for the bundles section parallel to the recipe skeleton so the section doesn't pop in after recipes have already loaded.

**Search bar (toggle-revealed)** — Toggle button in page-head reveals an input below the header; search filters both featured and grid; result count shown as faint text below input when query is active.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** When search is active and produces results, the 'Featured this week' section disappears (featured is set to undefined when isSearching). This is correct behaviour, but there is no visual explanation — the section silently vanishes, which can confuse users who were scrolled past the featured card.
  - *Fix:* No section change needed, but add a brief 'Searching all recipes' label above the result grid when isSearching is true, replacing the 'All recipes' h2, to make the scope clear.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The search input has no clear (×) button to reset. Users must manually select and delete the query to return to the full catalog. The result-count feedback line disappears when search is empty but the input stays visible, so there's no obvious 'done' affordance.
  - *Fix:* Add a clear button (×) inside the input when search.trim().length > 0. This is a standard pattern and avoids the extra click of closing the toggle.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The search bar has autoFocus on reveal, which is correct, but there is no keyboard shortcut to open the search toggle (e.g. pressing '/' or 'Cmd+F'). The toggle button has no visible keyboard shortcut hint.
  - *Fix:* Add a keydown listener on the section for '/' to open the search and focus the input, consistent with the pattern used in most developer-facing tools. This is a quality-of-life improvement for keyboard-primary users.

**Empty state** — EmptyState primitive used correctly for both 'no search results' and 'no recipes'; description copy varies by context.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The 'No recipes available' empty state description says 'The registry appears empty. Check your connection or try again later.' but at this point the page is already showing the hardcoded FALLBACK_REGISTRY (9 recipes). The true empty state (registry === null with no fallback) cannot realistically occur without also triggering the loadErr path. The description is slightly misleading.
  - *Fix:* Align with the actual code path: if totalVisible === 0 in non-searching mode and we have the fallback, show 'No recipes matched your filter' (with a reset link) or remove this state entirely since it can't be reached in normal operation.

**[...slug] Recipe Detail page** — Server-rendered; back link, page-head header, description, InstallPanel (client), ConnectorHealthPanel, Variables table, Steps summary, TrustMetadataCard, TrustDivergenceNotice, YamlPreview, TrustNote. Recoverable RegistryUnreachable error UI.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** TrustMetadataCard and TrustDivergenceNotice appear AFTER the full YAML preview in the rendered order. The YAML can be hundreds of lines long, burying the trust reconciliation warning below the fold. A user who installs without scrolling never sees the divergence notice.
  - *Fix:* Move TrustMetadataCard and TrustDivergenceNotice immediately above or below the InstallPanel, before the YamlPreview. The trust summary informs the install decision; it should appear before the raw source, not after.
- 🟡 **[med/M]** The Steps card shows only a count summary ('3 steps · 2 low risk · 1 medium risk') with no step names or descriptions. Users cannot evaluate risk without reading the raw YAML. The card exists between the description and the install button, setting a false expectation that it provides more detail.
  - *Fix:* Either expand the Steps card to list step ids/names (from the parsed YAML), or remove it and fold the risk counts into TrustMetadataCard's risk_level row as supplementary text ('low · 3 steps, 0 elevated').
- 🟡 **[med/M]** YamlPreview renders the full YAML with no syntax highlighting (plain pre tag with color: var(--ink-1)). For recipes with 50–150 lines, this is hard to audit. The submit page already imports YamlEditor (CodeMirror) client-side.
  - *Fix:* Wrap the YamlPreview pre in a client component that lazy-loads YamlEditor in read-only mode (same import path as the submit page), falling back to the plain pre on SSR. This adds zero new dependencies.

**bundle/[...slug] Bundle Detail page** — Same structural pattern as recipe detail: back link, BundleHeader, description, ManifestUnavailableNotice, WhatIsIncluded, ConnectorHealthPanel, TrustCard, RequiredEnvCard, BundleInstallPanel, TrustNote.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** ManifestUnavailableNotice (shown when manifest.json can't be fetched) uses role='status' but contains critical missing-data information ('specific recipe list, plugin name, policy template, and required env may be missing'). role='status' is polite/non-interruptive; this is important-enough information that role='alert' is more appropriate.
  - *Fix:* Change role='status' to role='alert' on ManifestUnavailableNotice to match the pattern used by the recipe detail's RegistryUnreachable and TrustDivergenceNotice.
- ⚪ **[low/M]** WhatIsIncluded lists recipe names as raw strings with underline-decorated mono links. When manifest is unavailable but bundle.recipe_count > 0, a count-only fallback ('3 recipes included') appears with no way to preview what those recipes are. The experience diverges sharply between manifest-available and manifest-unavailable states.
  - *Fix:* When manifest is null and recipe_count is known, add a link to the marketplace browse page filtered by the bundle name's tag, or show a 'View on GitHub' link to the install source directory, so users have a path to find out what's included.

**submit/page Submit a Recipe page** — Full compose form with metadata fields, preset/installed-recipe loader, YAML editor, lint validation, trust-consistency warnings, manifest preview, and a 2-step submitted view with copyable blocks.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The form layout uses gridTemplateColumns: '1fr' with className='recipe-submit-layout' but the CSS class presumably sets it to a 2-column layout at wider breakpoints (left: metadata, right: YAML). However the submit form comment says '-------- LEFT: metadata fields' and '-------- RIGHT: YAML editor', yet both divs sit inside a single 1fr grid column. If recipe-submit-layout doesn't override this, the form is stacked at all widths.
  - *Fix:* Verify recipe-submit-layout in the global CSS defines the 2-column responsive grid. If it does not, add gridTemplateColumns: 'repeat(auto-fit, minmax(320px, 1fr))' to the inline style so the metadata and YAML panels sit side-by-side on desktop as intended.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Trust metadata fields (risk level, approval behavior, network/file access checkboxes) use raw string option values ('always_ask', 'ask_on_novel', 'auto_approve') as option labels. These are internal enum keys, not readable labels. Compare with the browse page which maps them to 'Always asks', 'Asks on new', 'Auto'.
  - *Fix:* Use the same APPROVAL_LABEL map from the browse page (or a shared constant) as option display text. The value attribute can stay as the enum key; only the visible text needs to change.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The SubmittedView's step 2 instruction includes a warning in red (--err) text: 'Commit it to the SAME branch you used in step 1'. This is critical information but is styled with color: var(--err) inline on a strong tag inside a plain li, with no background or border to visually separate it. It reads as inline error text, not an advisory callout.
  - *Fix:* Extract the branch-check warning into a standalone warn-soft/warn-bordered div (matching the 'Branch check' notice already present below the ol), or use the existing HintCard pattern, so it reads as a deliberate callout rather than an error state within a list item.


### Approvals queue  `/approvals`

**Top 3:**
1. Replace the inline .alert-err div with the shared ErrorState primitive (adds role='alert', retry button, icon, and consistent framing) — currently a fetch failure silently degrades with no recovery path for the user
2. Make the BatchActionBar position:sticky at viewport bottom — batch-selecting cards at the top and having to scroll down to find the action buttons is a significant friction point for the primary multi-item workflow
3. Remove the redundant segment bar from RiskMeter so each ApprovalCard header shows a single RiskPill instead of bar + pill side-by-side — this recovers ~80px of horizontal header space on every card and eliminates the most visually cluttered element on the page

**Sub-nav (DecisionsTabs)** — cluster-tabs nav with Pending/Suggested/Knowledge tabs; pending count badge on Pending tab; sits at very top of section before the page header

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Nav renders above the page header (h1), inverting expected visual hierarchy — tab nav precedes any page identity or title
  - *Fix:* Move DecisionsTabs below the .page-head block so page title establishes context before section nav, matching pattern on other cluster pages
- 🟡 **[med/S]** No visible active-tab underline or strong weight difference is enforced by className alone ('cluster-tab is-active') — contrast of active vs inactive tab is entirely CSS-dependent and may wash out on light 'paper' theme if --line tokens are low-contrast
  - *Fix:* Add aria-current='page' (already present) and verify .is-active gets a bottom-border using --accent or --ink-1, not just --line-1, in both themes

**Page header (.page-head)** — h1 with serif editorial tagline, editorial-sub subtitle showing ~/.patchwork/inbox path + count + oldest timestamp, kbd-hint-row with KeyChip shortcuts and two plain Link destinations, a pending count pill, and a Sync inbox ghost button

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The h1 reads 'Approval queue — nothing leaves your machine without a nod.' — the serif tagline buries the actual queue count and wastes vertical space on every load; the signal (count) is demoted to a small pill in the flex end
  - *Fix:* Trim h1 to 'Approval queue' and promote the pending count or oldest-item age into the subtitle line; reserve editorial copy for the HintCard which users can dismiss
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The .kbd-hint-row contains two navigational links ('See approval patterns →' and 'Configure rules →') mixed with keyboard shortcut chips — conceptually different items sharing a single row with no visual separator beyond a · glyph, making it hard to scan
  - *Fix:* Split into two rows or use a flex gap + a border-left separator between shortcut chips and nav links; or move the links into the HintCard tip field so the hint row is purely shortcuts
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Sync inbox' button in the header has no aria-label and no disabled/loading state while the sync is in flight — a second tap can fire concurrent fetches
  - *Fix:* Add aria-label='Refresh approval inbox' and a loading state (Spinner + disabled) while the fetch is pending, matching the pattern used by Approve/Reject buttons

**HintCard** — Dismissable orange-accented aside rendered immediately below page header; uses HintCard primitive correctly

- ⚪ **[low/S]** HintCard renders between the header and the hero status card, adding a third content band before the user sees any queue data — on a narrow viewport this can push the first ApprovalCard below the fold
  - *Fix:* Conditionally render HintCard only when the queue is empty (alongside the EmptyState) so it doesn't compete with live approval data for above-the-fold space

**Hero status card (.apq-hero-card)** — Card with bespoke Queue label + awaiting-decision count, a four-stat row (Total/High/Medium/Low), and a historical approval-rate bar with percentage pills; only rendered when pending.length > 0

- 🟡 **[med/M]** The four stats (Total, High, Medium, Low) are custom bespoke divs with .apq-stat / .apq-stat-value / .apq-stat-label classes rather than the shared StatCard primitive — duplicates visual pattern already established elsewhere in the dashboard
  - *Fix:* Replace the .apq-stats row with four StatCard components (or a 4-column grid of the GlassCard inner pattern) to pick up consistent typography, spacing, and hover states without custom CSS
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The historical-rate bar uses two plain divs (.apq-rate-fill-ok / .apq-rate-fill-err) with inline width% style and separate pill labels — the pills repeat the same percentages already visible in the bar, creating redundancy, and neither element has an explicit height or border-radius token
  - *Fix:* Remove the redundant percentage pills; keep only the bar with the existing aria-label. Render the bar height via --s-2 and border-radius via --r-s so it stays consistent with other meter components
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Queue' section label and count ('X awaiting decision') duplicate the pending count pill already in the .page-head — users see the same number three times (h1 subtitle, page-head pill, hero card)
  - *Fix:* Remove the .apq-queue sub-block entirely; the hero card's value is in the per-tier breakdown, not restating the total that is already in the header

**Filter bar (.filter-chips)** — Four toggle buttons (All/Low/Medium/High) with counts, aria-pressed, URL sync; only shown when queue is non-empty

- ⚪ **[low/S]** Filter chip labels for risk tiers are plain text ('Low', 'Medium', 'High') without any color cue — a user switching from the tier-colored hero stats to the filter bar gets no visual continuity between the two
  - *Fix:* Add a small colored dot (matching RiskPill dot colors: --green/--amber/--red) before each non-All chip label to echo the color language already established in RiskMeter and RiskPill
- 🟡 **[med/S]** When a filter is active and produces zero results, the empty state reads 'No X-risk approvals pending' but the filter chip remains selected with count '0' and no visual indication the filter is active — users may think the page is broken
  - *Fix:* Apply a distinct active style (e.g. border using --accent-cool, or background using the tier's semantic soft color) to the active chip so the filtered state is immediately visible; already have aria-pressed, just needs CSS

**Error banner (.alert-err)** — Simple div.alert-err with plain text 'Unreachable: {err}'; rendered inline in the flow whenever err state is set; no retry action, no icon

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The inline .alert-err div is a bespoke element rather than the shared ErrorState primitive — missing icon, role='alert', retry affordance, and the consistent visual framing from ErrorState
  - *Fix:* Replace with ErrorState component: pass error={err}, title='Could not reach bridge', onRetry pointing to the same manual fetch logic used by the Sync button
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The error div appears mid-page between the filter bar and session filter banner, not at the top of the content area — a user may scroll past it before noticing the queue data is stale
  - *Fix:* Move the error display to immediately below the filter bar (or above it) and ensure role='alert' so screen readers announce it; ErrorState already has role='alert'

**Session / recipe filter banners** — Two distinct inline banners (.alert-info for session filter, .apq-recipe-filter for recipe filter) with different visual treatments; recipe filter has a note explaining approvals don't carry recipe IDs

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The recipe filter banner renders an explanatory note in muted text ('approval payloads don't carry a recipe identifier — showing all pending approvals') but the filter is still applied with no visual differentiation from a real filter — this is misleading UX
  - *Fix:* If the recipe filter has no backend effect, disable the filter chip entirely rather than showing a banner with a caveat; if kept, add a warn-tone icon to the banner so users immediately see the filter is nominal
- ⚪ **[low/S]** Session filter uses .alert-info class and recipe filter uses .apq-recipe-filter — two different CSS classes for structurally equivalent 'active filter' banners
  - *Fix:* Unify both into a single .active-filter-banner class (or use the shared pill pattern with a Clear button) so the visual treatment is consistent

**Select-all row + ApprovalCard list** — Optional 'Select all' row (checkbox + label) above .approval-list; each ApprovalCard is an article.card.apc with header (checkbox, icon, h3, RiskMeter, pills, countdown), optional summary, signal chips, primary param, params toggle, code/diff block, decision buttons, copy actions

- 🔴 **[high/S]** RiskMeter renders both a bar-graph visual (4 segments) AND a RiskPill chip — two redundant risk indicators side by side in the card header, consuming ~80px of horizontal space on every card. The bar-graph adds no information the RiskPill text doesn't already convey
  - *Fix:* Remove the segmented bar from RiskMeter and keep only the RiskPill; or remove RiskPill from RiskMeter and let the bar stand alone with its existing aria-label — choose one representation per card
- 🟡 **[med/S]** riskSignals and personalSignals are both rendered inside .apc-signals divs with identical className logic and no visual separator or heading between them — a card with both sets looks like one undifferentiated chip row, losing the conceptual distinction the comment in the code carefully documents
