- ⚪ **[low/S]** The description embeds a backtick-escaped CLI command (`patchwork suggest`) as plain text inside a template literal. It renders without monospace formatting in the browser, making the command indistinguishable from prose.
  - *Fix:* Wrap the command in a `<code>` element inside the description prop, or use the EmptyState's `action` prop to render a CTA button linking to /suggestions rather than embedding CLI instructions in body copy.

**Tool history table (card wrapper, header, sortable columns)** — A .card container with card-head h2 + count pill, then a horizontally-scrollable table with 7 columns: Tool (with severity pill), Heuristic, Matched rule, approvals (✓), rejections (✗), Rate (visual bar), Last.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The 'Rate' column header (line 460) links to a visual bar but the column heading just says 'Rate' — there is no percentage text rendered alongside the bar. A user sorting by Rate has no numeric anchor to compare rows, only relative bar widths at 80px wide.
  - *Fix:* Render the approval rate as a percentage text immediately before or after the bar (e.g. '94%' in --fs-xs tabular-nums), then the bar becomes a visual supplement rather than the only data. The approvalRate field on ToolInsight already provides the value.
- 🔴 **[high/S]** The ✓ and ✗ column headers (lines 429, 445) are single-character glyphs with tooltip titles — but those tooltips only appear on pointer hover. Screen-reader users and keyboard users get no header label identifying these columns.
  - *Fix:* Add visually-hidden text inside the th elements: `<span className='sr-only'>Approvals</span>` after the ✓ glyph, and similarly for ✗ Rejections. Also add `scope='col'` to all th elements for proper table semantics.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Table has no `<caption>` or `aria-label`. Screen readers announce it as 'table' with no context. The table also has 7 columns including two narrow numeric columns (✓/✗) and a Heuristic column with maxWidth 260px — on viewports below 900px, horizontal scroll engages silently with no visual affordance.
  - *Fix:* Add `<caption className='sr-only'>Tool approval history</caption>` as the first child of the table element. For mobile, consider hiding the Heuristic column below 768px via a CSS media query, since the severity pill in the Tool column already conveys the same categorical signal.

**Table rows (tool chip, heuristic label, RuleCell, counts, bar, timestamp)** — Each row: severity pill + code link to /activity, heuristic text (--ink-2, maxWidth 260), RuleCell (async-loaded matched rule + tier/source pills), approval count (--ok colored link), rejection count (--err or --ink-3 colored link), 80px approval bar, relative timestamp.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** Tool names in the Tool column are plain `<code>` elements (--fs-s = 12px) with no truncation. Long namespaced tool names (e.g. 'mcp__claude-ide-bridge__generateAPIDocumentation') will overflow their cell and push adjacent columns off-screen on any viewport.
  - *Fix:* Add `style={{ maxWidth: 220, overflow: 'hidden', textOverflow: 'ellipsis', whiteSpace: 'nowrap' }}` to the code element, and expose the full tool name via the existing `title` prop on the Link wrapper — it already has `title={\`View ${t.toolName} activity\`}`.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The RuleCell renders a loading state as a plain '…' span in --ink-3 at --fs-xs (11px). This 11px faint ellipsis is invisible at normal reading distance and provides no indication to the user that content is loading in this column.
  - *Fix:* Replace the '…' loading placeholder in RuleCell (line 119) with a small `<Skeleton>` inline block (e.g. `<Skeleton style={{ width: 80, height: 14 }} />`) to communicate the async load and match the loading pattern used elsewhere in the dashboard.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Last' column timestamp (relativeTime) is colored --ink-3 (faintest text token) at implied --fs-m (13px). At --ink-3 contrast on --bg-1, this falls below WCAG AA for small text. The column is also right-aligned with zero padding on the right (padding: '10px 0'), so on narrow viewports the timestamp clips against the card edge.
  - *Fix:* Bump the timestamp color to --ink-2 for sufficient contrast. Add at minimum `paddingRight: 'var(--s-2)'` to the Last td so text doesn't abut the card border. The table already has `overflowX: auto` on the wrapper, but inner padding prevents visual clipping.

**Footer / metadata line** — A <p> tag below the table, --fs-xs / --ink-2, showing generated timestamp and a privacy note ('nothing leaves your machine').

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The timestamp is formatted with toLocaleTimeString() — time-only, no date. If the page is open after midnight or the data is from a prior session, '2:14:03 AM' is ambiguous without a date.
  - *Fix:* Use `toLocaleString()` or format as 'Today at 2:14 AM' / 'Jun 24 at 2:14 AM' to disambiguate cross-day staleness. Alternatively use the existing relativeTime helper on generatedAt.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The privacy note ('nothing leaves your machine') is valuable but currently buried in --fs-xs --ink-2 at the bottom of a scrollable page. First-time users who are hesitant about the page never see it.
  - *Fix:* Move the privacy note into the editorial-sub subtitle in the page-head (one sentence, already --ink-2 and visible before scrolling), and remove it from the footer to avoid duplication.


### Insights Replay  `/insights/replay`

**Top 3:**
1. Replace raw div.alert-err with the shared ErrorState component to gain role='alert', a retry action, and accessible error presentation — currently the only error surface on the page is an unstyled banner with no recovery path.
2. Raise decision pill font-size from var(--fs-2xs) / 10px to at minimum var(--fs-xs) / 11px across all table cells — the 'Was', 'Would be', and 'Change' pills are the primary scannable data on this page and are currently below WCAG minimum text size, especially the 'Change' column which is the entire point of the replay.
3. Replace the inline empty-table-state paragraph ('No changed decisions in this window…') with the shared EmptyState primitive — the page currently has three visually inconsistent empty states (EmptyState, a raw paragraph, and a divergence-free inline banner), creating a fragmented and unpolished feel.

**Page Header** — page-head flex row: left=BackLink + h1 + page-head-sub description paragraph; right=Lookback label+select+conditional pills. Wraps on narrow viewports.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** page-head aligns to flex-end (baseline of tallest child), so the right-side controls mis-align against the h1 baseline on wide viewports — the lookback label and pills sit too low relative to the page title.
  - *Fix:* Change the outer page-head div's alignItems to 'flex-start' (or keep flex-end but anchor only the controls div to self-align center). Controls should top-align with the h1 row, not float to the bottom of the description paragraph.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The description paragraph (page-head-sub) is very long — 40+ words — and opens with 'What would have happened if…', a rhetorical question that buries the operative fact (this is a policy diff tool, read-only). On scan, users see the question before understanding the value.
  - *Fix:* Lead with the action: 'Re-evaluates historical approvals against today\'s policy — read-only, no tools re-executed.' Cut the rhetorical opening clause.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The right-side summary pills (total decisions, changed, now-allowed, now-denied) appear conditionally after data loads, causing a layout shift that pushes the lookback select leftward when pills appear. They also share a flat flex row with the select, giving equal weight to controls and summary stats.
  - *Fix:* Visually separate the filter controls from the summary pills with a subtle divider (e.g. a 1px var(--line-1) separator or gap difference). Keep the pills in a stable reserved slot so they don\'t cause horizontal shift on load.

**Loading State** — SkeletonList rows=6 columns=4 shown when loading and no cached rows.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** SkeletonList with columns=4 doesn\'t match the actual 5-column table layout (Tool, Was, Would be, Change, When), so the skeleton and real content have different widths and the transition is jarring.
  - *Fix:* Pass columns={5} to SkeletonList to match the real table structure.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The divergence-free banner (ok-soft box, '✓ Your current policy matches…') and the stat pills in the header both lack skeleton placeholders during initial load, so the page reads as 'no data' before load completes rather than 'loading'.
  - *Fix:* Wrap the header pills zone in a conditional that shows a SkeletonStatCard or two small skeleton pills while loading && !data. Avoids the double-empty impression.

**Error State** — Raw div.alert-err with the error string inline: 'Unreachable: {error}'.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The error state uses the bare .alert-err div instead of the shared ErrorState component. ErrorState adds role='alert', a centered icon, readable prose title, mono detail block, and optional Retry — the raw div has none of these, missing a11y + retry affordance.
  - *Fix:* Replace `<div className="alert-err">Unreachable: {error}</div>` with `<ErrorState title="Could not load replay data" error={error} onRetry={() => window.location.reload()} />`. Import ErrorState from @/components/patchwork (it\'s already imported via the EmptyState import line — add it there).

**Empty State (no history)** — EmptyState component with title and description when totalRows===0. Correct primitive usage.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** EmptyState description says 'Widen the lookback or come back after the bridge has processed some approval decisions.' — when the user is on 90-day lookback, 'Widen the lookback' is unhelpful advice. There\'s also no link to the policy page where they can start making decisions.
  - *Fix:* Make the description context-sensitive: when sinceDays === 90, omit the lookback suggestion. Add an action link: `action={<Link href='/insights'>Back to Approval Insights</Link>}` so users have a next step.

**Divergence-Free Banner** — Inline-styled div with ok-soft background and border when changedCount===0. Shows '✓ Your current policy matches all N historical decisions — no divergence detected.'

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The banner is constructed with raw inline styles (padding, borderRadius, background, border, fontSize, marginBottom all inline) instead of the .alert-ok or .alert-err CSS class pattern used elsewhere, and does not map to any shared primitive (HintCard is available in patchwork/).
  - *Fix:* Replace the div with `<HintCard tone="ok">` or at minimum swap the inline styles for a .alert-ok utility class (define it alongside .alert-err in globals.css if it doesn\'t exist). Keeps visual language consistent with alert-warn/alert-err.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The checkmark '✓' is a raw text character with no aria-hidden or sr-only label. Screen readers may announce it as 'check mark' interrupting the message.
  - *Fix:* Wrap the ✓ in `<span aria-hidden="true">✓ </span>` so the icon is purely decorative; the sentence text carries the meaning.

**Table Card Header (card-head)** — card-head flex row: left=h2 with dynamic title ('Changed decisions (N)' / 'All decisions (N)'); right=checkbox label 'Show unchanged'.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The h2 title flips between 'Changed decisions' and 'All decisions' as the toggle changes, which is confusing — the toggle already signals the mode. The heading redundantly describes the toggle state rather than naming the section.
  - *Fix:* Fix the h2 to 'Decision log' and move the count into a small .pill.muted beside it: `<h2>Decision log <span class="pill muted">{visible.length}</span></h2>`. The toggle label already explains what\'s being shown.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The 'Show unchanged' checkbox label has no id/htmlFor pairing — it uses a wrapping label element which is valid HTML, but the `<input>` has no id and there\'s no aria-label on it. Screen readers will announce it only if the wrapping label is recognised.
  - *Fix:* Add `id="show-unchanged"` to the input and `htmlFor="show-unchanged"` to the label wrapper — belt-and-suspenders for assistive tech, matching the pattern already used on the since-days select.

**Results Table** — Full-width HTML table with 5 columns (Tool, Was, Would be, Change, When). Changed rows highlighted with var(--warn-soft) background. Pills use var(--fs-2xs) = 10px.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** Decision pills in 'Was' and 'Would be' columns use var(--fs-2xs) = 10px, which is below the 11px WCAG minimum for supplementary text and will fail contrast on some pill background combos. The 'Change' column pill also at 10px is the most important signal on changed rows.
  - *Fix:* Raise all row-level pill font-size to var(--fs-xs) (11px) minimum. The 'Change' column pill should be var(--fs-s) (12px) since it\'s the primary scannable signal.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Was' → 'Would be' column naming requires cognitive parsing. A user scanning quickly reads left-to-right: 'Was … Would be … Change' — the Change column is redundant with the colour difference between Was and Would be, but Was/Would be alone aren\'t scannable at a glance.
  - *Fix:* Rename columns to 'Original' and 'Replayed' — shorter, unambiguous, technical vocabulary appropriate for this audience. Keep 'Change' column as the diff signal.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Unchanged rows (when Show unchanged is toggled on) have no visual differentiation from changed rows other than the absence of warn-soft background. In a long list they blend together, making it hard to spot changed rows.
  - *Fix:* Add `opacity: 0.55` or `color: var(--ink-2)` to unchanged rows (when showUnchanged mode) so changed rows (which retain full opacity and warn-soft) stand out clearly by contrast.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The table has no aria-label or caption element. A screen reader user arriving at the table hears 'table' with no context about what it contains.
  - *Fix:* Add `aria-label="Decision replay results"` to the `<table>` element.

**Empty Table State (no changed decisions, toggle off)** — Inline paragraph with --fs-m text: 'No changed decisions in this window. Toggle "Show unchanged" to see all rows.'

- 🟡 **[med/S]** This inline paragraph is a third empty-state variant in the page (alongside EmptyState component and the divergence-free banner) and uses raw inline styles instead of the EmptyState primitive. It sits inside the card with no vertical centering, reading as a stray line of body text rather than a deliberate empty state.
  - *Fix:* Replace the `<p>` with `<EmptyState title="No changed decisions" description="Toggle 'Show unchanged' to view all {rows.length} decisions in this window." />` inside the card body. Consistent visual language with the no-history EmptyState.

**Footer / Metadata Row** — Conditional paragraph below the card: workspace path in code, 'Generated at {time}' in locale time string.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** 'Generated at 14:32:07' — locale time string with no date. If the page is left open and revisited next morning, the time is ambiguous without the date. The 60s polling interval also means data can be up to 60s stale without any indication.
  - *Fix:* Show relative time matching the pattern used in the table: 'Generated 2m ago · {workspace}' using the already-defined relativeTime(data.generatedAt). More useful than an absolute clock time.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The workspace code element uses var(--fs-2xs) = 10px which is too small for a path string that may be 40–60 characters. At narrow viewports it will overflow horizontally.
  - *Fix:* Raise to var(--fs-xs) (11px) and add `word-break: break-all` so long paths wrap gracefully.


### Connections  `/connections`

**Top 3:**
1. Collapse the duplicate disconnect affordance in ConnectorGridCard: the toggle switch (role='switch') and the 'Disconnect' text button both invoke the same action in the same card footer — remove the redundant button, which also resolves the role='switch' misuse and reduces visual noise on every connected card.
2. Co-locate the search input and filter pills into a single filter bar row below the page header — the current split (search in page-head toolbar, pills below the empty-state CTA) makes the two controls appear unrelated and breaks the spatial model for filtering the catalog.
3. Replace unlabeled primary token inputs in the PAT/Notion modals with proper <label> elements — placeholder-only labeling disappears on typing, fails WCAG 1.3.1, and breaks browser autofill, affecting every user who connects a PAT-based service.

**Header / Hero** — editorial-h1 with inline accent span 'writes are gated. Reads are not.' + small-caps subtitle listing 'oauth · scoped to your machine · tokens in ~/.patchwork/secrets' + RelationStrip cross-links

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The h1 embeds a policy statement as decorative serif accent copy ('writes are gated. Reads are not.') — it reads as a tagline, not a signal. Users scanning for status or action land on an opaque slogan before seeing any data.
  - *Fix:* Move the policy note to a HintCard (one already exists: <HintCard id='connections' />) or a small muted pill beneath the title. The h1 should be simply 'Connections' so the page name is unambiguous at a glance.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The subtitle 'oauth · scoped to your machine · tokens in ~/.patchwork/secrets' uses --ink-3 (faint) styling and dot-separated fragments with zero structure — a filesystem path is not useful to most users here, and the combination makes the line feel like debug metadata rather than helpful orientation.
  - *Fix:* Replace with a single declarative sentence at --ink-2 weight: 'Connect services to give recipes read (and optionally write) access.' Drop the raw path — it belongs in the HintCard detail only.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The toolbar (search input + Re-auth all button) is conditionally rendered only when !loading && !bridgeOffline, but its container class 'conn-toolbar' has no aria-label and no role. When Re-auth all is disabled (0 targets) the button has no visual disabled style described — relies on the generic btn.disabled state.
  - *Fix:* Wrap toolbar in a <div role='toolbar' aria-label='Connector controls'>. No behavior change needed — just the semantic wrapper so screen readers announce the region.

**Filter Bar (status pills + search)** — Four pill-buttons (All [N], Connected [N], Available [N], Coming soon [N]) rendered as className='pill info|muted conn-filter-pill'; search input floats in the page-head toolbar above, spatially separated from the pills it filters

- 🔴 **[high/M]** Search input lives inside .page-head (top toolbar) while the filter pills live below the empty-state CTA — they control the same visible catalog but are spatially disjoint. A user who types in the search box has no visual cue that the pills below also refine results, and vice versa.
  - *Fix:* Move the search input into the same .conn-filter-pills row (left side), so filters and search are co-located. Give the row role='search' and aria-label='Filter connectors'.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** Filter pill labels embed counts in square brackets: 'Connected [3]' — the bracket syntax is unconventional and visually noisy. Count is also recomputed every render but never updates live after connect/disconnect without a full page reload of the pill area.
  - *Fix:* Use a standard badge span inside the pill: 'Connected <span class="pill-count">3</span>' — consistent with how StatCard and AnalyticsTabs elsewhere render counts. Counts already update via setConnectors so the value is correct; just clean up the bracket syntax.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Pills have no aria-pressed or aria-current attribute — the active state is conveyed only via className switch (pill info vs pill muted), which means screen readers cannot distinguish the selected filter.
  - *Fix:* Add aria-pressed={statusFilter === k} to each pill button.

**Recently Used Strip** — Horizontal scroll row of up to 4 glass-card--hover RecentCards (40px LogoTile + name + '✓ Xm ago') shown only when 1+ connectors have lastSync; section label 'Recently used' in plain div text

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The checkmark '✓' prefix on .conn-recent-sync is a raw Unicode character with no aria-hidden — screen readers will announce 'check mark 3 minutes ago'. The relative time alone is sufficient.
  - *Fix:* Replace '✓ {relativeTime(lastSync)}' with '<span aria-hidden="true">✓</span> <time dateTime={lastSync}>{relativeTime(lastSync)}</time>' — or drop the checkmark entirely and rely on card position in the 'Recently used' section to imply success.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** RecentCards are not interactive — they show the connector name and last sync but clicking does nothing. Users may expect clicking to jump to that connector's card in the grid below, especially when the grid is long.
  - *Fix:* Wrap the RecentCard in an anchor or button that scrolls/focuses the matching .cgc-card in the grid (via id='conn-card-{def.id}' + scrollIntoView). Minimal effort, high discoverability payoff.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The section header 'Recently used' is a plain unstyled div with class 'conn-recent-label' — its font weight/size is unspecified in this file and likely relies on a global CSS class. There is no aria-label or heading role on the section, so the strip has no landmark association for screen readers.
  - *Fix:* Change to <h2 className='conn-recent-label'> or add role='region' aria-label='Recently used connectors' on the .conn-recent-section wrapper.

**Empty State (no connections yet)** — Custom inline-styled dashed-border CTA box with emoji plug icon, heading 'No connections yet', subtext, and a '+ Add connection' primary button — does NOT use the shared <EmptyState> primitive

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The empty-state CTA uses a raw emoji (🔌) inside a hand-rolled circle div with inline rgba() color mixing (rgba(var(--accent-rgb, 99, 102, 241), 0.1)) — --accent-rgb is not a documented design token. On some themes this produces a fallback purple that may not match --accent (orange). The EmptyState primitive already handles icon + title + body + CTA consistently.
  - *Fix:* Replace the entire .conn-empty-cta block with <EmptyState title='No connections yet' description='Connect a service to start automating with recipes.' action={<button className="btn primary" onClick={() => setModalOpen(true)}>+ Add connection</button>} />. Retire the inline styles.
- 🔴 **[high/S]** The empty state and the full catalog grid are both visible simultaneously — when hasAnyConnected is false the user sees the empty-state CTA immediately above the full 47-item Available catalog. The CTA says 'No connections yet' while the grid shows 47 items to connect, which is redundant and visually cluttered.
  - *Fix:* Show the empty-state CTA only when the visibleCatalog after filtering is also empty (e.g., a search returns 0 results). When there are available connectors, skip the CTA — the grid with Connect buttons is the CTA.

**Connector Grid (ConnectorGridCard)** — Responsive CSS grid of .cgc-card cards; each shows 48px LogoTile with pulsing green dot overlay when connected, name, category, status pill, scope chips or tool count, optional recipe count badge, test result, footer with toggle+Test+Disconnect or Connect button; status grouping under 'Connected (N)' / 'Available (N)' section headings when filter=all

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Connect' button on disconnected cards and the 'Disconnect' button in the footer both lack visible focus rings beyond the browser default — the cgc-action-btn and cgc-connect-btn classes are not described as having a :focus-visible outline in this file. For a page full of interactive cards, tab navigation is error-prone.
  - *Fix:* Ensure .cgc-connect-btn:focus-visible and .cgc-action-btn:focus-visible apply a 2px --accent outline with 2px offset, consistent with global btn:focus-visible. Audit in the CSS file.
- 🔴 **[high/M]** The 'Disconnect' button inside the footer of a connected card uses role='switch' aria-checked={true} for the toggle icon, but simultaneously renders a separate cgc-action-btn also labeled 'Disconnect' — two elements in the same card footer both invoke disconnect with no visual hierarchy between them. The switch toggle and the text button duplicate the same action.
  - *Fix:* Pick one affordance: keep the toggle switch (role='switch') for disconnect, remove the redundant cgc-action-btn 'Disconnect' text button. Reserve the text button slot for a secondary action (e.g., 'Re-auth'). For degraded state, the 'Reconnect' text button is the correct primary CTA — keep that.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Section headers 'Connected (N)' and 'Available (N)' inside the grid rendering block are plain inline-styled divs — not headings, not landmarks. The Connected header uses --ok green which is meaningful but the Available header uses --ink-3 (faint gray) making it visually subordinate to body text. Neither has a role or id.
  - *Fix:* Change both to <h2> or <h3> elements with appropriate className. Give Connected section a role='region' aria-label='Connected connectors' wrapper div. Consistent heading hierarchy helps both sighted scanning and screen readers.

**ConnectorHealthPanel (used in recipe context, not on this page directly)** — glass-card with 'Required connectors' h3, summary pills (total/ok/degraded/issues), per-connector rows with 8px dot + monospace name + status label + optional message truncated at 200px + Connect link routing to /connections; 30s polling; fetchErr inline beside header; loading shown as plain 'Loading…' text span

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The loading state renders as a plain <span style={{ color: 'var(--ink-3)' }}>Loading…</span> with no skeleton — inconsistent with the Connections page which uses <SkeletonList> and the rest of the dashboard which uses SkeletonStatCard/Skeleton primitives.
  - *Fix:* Replace the loading span with <SkeletonList rows={connectors.length || 2} /> inside the panel body while statusMap === null && !fetchErr.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 'Connect' button link inside each row routes to the generic /connections page, not to the specific connector. When a recipe needs 'slack' and it's missing, clicking 'Connect' drops the user on the full 47-connector catalog with no scroll position or focus on Slack.
  - *Fix:* Route to /connections#conn-card-{name.toLowerCase()} (pending the anchor id fix in the grid) or pass a ?highlight=slack query param. Even without deep-linking, this is a zero-effort improvement: href={`/connections?q=${encodeURIComponent(name)}`} pre-fills the search box.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The connector name in each panel row uses font-mono at --fs-s which renders smaller than the surrounding UI (--fs-m body). For a panel labeled 'Required connectors', the name is the most important piece of information and should not read as secondary metadata.
  - *Fix:* Use font-sans at --fs-m (or --fs-s with fontWeight: 500) for the connector name. Reserve mono only for token/path values, not human-readable service names.

**ConnectorBadgeRow (used in recipe cards elsewhere)** — Row of up to 2 16x16px connector glyphs (SVG mask or 7px initials in bg-2 box) + overflow '+N' badge; glyph set covers 14 connectors via KNOWN_SVGS, others fall back to two-letter initials

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The outer wrapper span for each glyph (lines 68-85) has no title or aria-label on the outer span itself — the inner ConnectorGlyph adds aria-label only for SVG variants. The initials fallback has no accessible label at all. When only initials show (e.g., 'DD' for Datadog) screen readers announce nothing meaningful.
  - *Fix:* Add aria-label={c} to the outer wrapper span consistently, replacing the current approach where only the inner SVG span has aria-label={id}. This ensures both SVG and initials variants are announced.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The overflow badge '+{overflow}' uses color-mix(in srgb, var(--accent-cool) 15%, transparent) which is not available in all browsers that support the rest of the token system; Safari < 16.2 will render this as transparent.
  - *Fix:* Replace with a CSS variable alias or use rgba fallback: background: 'var(--accent-cool-10, rgba(99,179,237,0.15))'. Define --accent-cool-10 in the token sheet alongside the other semantic tokens.

**Token / OAuth Modals (Notion, generic PAT, Disconnect confirm, Re-auth confirm)** — Four Dialog instances sharing .conn-modal-body layout; PAT modals use password inputs with placeholder text as only label for primary field; Notion modal uses type='password' with placeholder 'secret_...'; generic modal labels extras via htmlFor but primary token input has only aria-label derived from placeholder text; Cancel buttons alternate between .conn-modal-cancel and .conn-modal-cancel-sm inconsistently

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The primary token <input type='password'> in both the Notion modal and the generic PAT modal has no <label> element — it relies solely on the aria-label prop set to the placeholder concatenation. Placeholder text disappears on input, leaving the field unlabeled visually once the user starts typing. This also breaks autofill heuristics.
  - *Fix:* Add a visually-hidden <label htmlFor='notion-token-input'>Notion integration token</label> (or generic equivalent) above each primary input, matching the pattern already used for extraFields inputs.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** Cancel button styling is inconsistent: Notion/PAT modals use .conn-modal-cancel (custom class), Re-auth confirm uses .btn.sm.ghost, Disconnect confirm uses .conn-modal-cancel-sm — three different class patterns for the same semantic action across four modals.
  - *Fix:* Standardize all Cancel buttons to className='btn sm ghost' — the ghost variant already exists, matches the design system, and is used correctly in Re-auth confirm. Remove .conn-modal-cancel and .conn-modal-cancel-sm custom classes.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The Re-auth confirmation list (conn-reauth-list) renders raw connector IDs ('github', 'google-calendar') as <li> text — not display names. Users who connected 'Google Calendar' will see 'google-calendar' in the confirmation, which is inconsistent with how the connector appears everywhere else on the page.
  - *Fix:* Resolve display names from CATALOG: reAuthTargets.map(c => CATALOG.find(d => d.id === c.id)?.name ?? c.id). One lookup, no data changes.

**Loading / Error / Offline States** — <SkeletonList rows={3} columns={2} /> for initial load; <EmptyState> for bridgeOffline; raw <div className='alert-err'> for the err string (shown even when bridgeOffline EmptyState is also visible); no error state for partial fetch failures mid-session

- 🟡 **[med/S]** When bridgeOffline is true, the component renders both the <EmptyState title='Bridge offline'> AND potentially the <div class='alert-err'> for err (lines 1751-1754). Both describe the same failure. The alert-err fires unconditionally before the bridgeOffline guard, so a user sees two error messages stacked.
  - *Fix:* Suppress the alert-err when bridgeOffline is true: {err && !bridgeOffline && <div className='alert-err' role='alert'>{err}</div>}.
- ⚪ **[low/M]** The SkeletonList uses rows={3} columns={2} regardless of the CATALOG size (47 items) — the skeleton implies a small 6-item list but the real content is a dense grid of 47+ cards. The transition from skeleton to grid is jarring in layout shift and does not reflect actual content shape.
  - *Fix:* Use a SkeletonList that mimics the grid: either render 6-8 skeleton cards in the .conn-grid class directly, or use a generic 2-column grid skeleton that matches the cgc-card height. Alternatively, show the filter pills immediately and skeleton only the grid area.


### Settings  `/settings`

**Top 3:**
1. Add aria role='navigation' + aria-label to the side nav and replace the kill-switch's emoji-only engaged signal with an aria-live announcement — two accessibility gaps on the most safety-critical section of the page.
2. Replace per-card empty/null states (stats bar '—', permission grid 'No data', driver list defaults) with Skeleton primitives so users can distinguish bridge-offline from still-loading — currently both states look identical.
3. Remove the decorative serif .accent tagline from the page h1 ('config that lives in plaintext.') which buries the actual config path, and reorder the delegation-policy select options to lead with human meaning before the internal key ('No gating (off)' not 'off — no gating').

**Page Header** — Two-part row: editorial-h1 with italic serif accent tagline + stg-save-indicator flash on the right; subtitle shows config file path + 'changes hot-reload'.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The .accent span ('config that lives in plaintext.') renders as neutral --ink-2 italic serif per the facelift rule — it no longer earns emphasis and reads as decorative noise that buries the real signal (the config path). The actual path is already in the subtitle immediately below, making the tagline redundant.
  - *Fix:* Remove the <span class="accent"> tagline entirely. Move the config path up to sit directly in the h1 as a secondary label or mono suffix, so the header leads with the config path signal rather than a decorative phrase.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The .editorial-sub shows configPath + '· changes hot-reload' in a single truncated line (white-space: nowrap, text-overflow: ellipsis on desktop). A long path like /Users/you/Documents/Projects/foo truncates the 'changes hot-reload' hint entirely, hiding the UX affordance.
  - *Fix:* Put the config path in a separate mono element (use the .mono-path style already in globals.css) and place 'changes hot-reload' on its own line or as a StatusPill tone='ok' badge, not in the same truncated editorial-sub.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The stg-save-indicator ('Saved' flash) appears only when saving — the idle state is invisible (opacity: 0). If the save fails mid-navigation the user has no persistent success/failure record. Error outcomes from individual save actions are only shown inline per-section; there is no page-level error summary.
  - *Fix:* On error, keep the stg-save-indicator visible with err color (using --err token) and a brief 'Save failed' label until the next successful save, so the page header acts as a triage point. Do not require the user to scroll to find which section errored.

**Sticky Side Nav** — 200px sticky left column with stg-nav-link items + ConfigFileCard below; active link highlighted with --orange-soft background + --accent text; mobile collapses to horizontal chip row.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The side nav has no ARIA role or aria-label. Screen readers encounter six anchor links with no landmark context — they are not announced as navigation.
  - *Fix:* Add role='navigation' and aria-label='Settings sections' to the <nav> element. The stg-nav-link anchors already have meaningful text so no aria-label needed on the links themselves.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** ConfigFileCard sits below the nav in the sticky column. Its stg-config-copy-btn has a rendered height of ~22px (padding: 3px 8px, fs-xs ~11px) — flagged in the globals.css comment at line 8766 as 'very small'. On a track-pad or touch screen the tap target is under the 44px WCAG minimum.
  - *Fix:* Apply min-height: 32px and padding-block: 6px to .stg-config-copy-btn, matching the corrective rule already added for stg-action-btn (line 8809). Reuse the existing .stg-config-copy-btn block at line 8830 in the desktop fix section and add it to the mobile fix section at line 8450 as well.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The mobile chip row uses flex-wrap: wrap but there is no visual scroll indicator or padding at the right edge, so wrapped chips look cut off on 375px viewports.
  - *Fix:* Add padding-right: var(--s-3) to .settings-grid > nav .stg-nav-list and apply overflow-x: auto only when chips do NOT wrap (or cap at one row with overflow-x: auto, overflow-y: hidden). Alternatively allow wrapping but add gap: var(--s-2) and a thin --line-1 bottom border to separate from the card stack below.

**Bridge Card (s-bridge)** — card with card-head containing h2 + subtitle + StatusPill (extension connected/offline), three read-only stg-input fields, stg-readonly-note, and a stg-stats-bar footer row (mode, sessions, uptime).

- 🟡 **[med/S]** All three form inputs (workspace path, inbox dir, bridge port) are read-only but styled identically to editable inputs via .stg-input — they have opacity: 0.7 and cursor: default, but no visual cue that they are informational. Users routinely click them expecting to edit.
  - *Fix:* Replace the read-only inputs with <div class='stg-stat-val mono'> elements or use a definition-list layout (dl/dt/dd) for clarity. If the input element is kept for copy accessibility, add a <span class='stg-readonly-badge'>read-only</span> badge beside each label matching the existing .stg-readonly-note pattern.
- 🟡 **[med/M]** The stg-stats-bar (Mode / Sessions / Uptime) renders as unlabeled text fragments using --ink-2 for labels and --ink-0 .stg-stat-val for values. Before /status resolves, Sessions shows '0' and Uptime shows '—' — indistinguishable from the loaded state. Users cannot tell if the bridge is offline or just slow.
  - *Fix:* Replace with three SkeletonStatCard placeholders while settings is null, falling back to real values once loaded. Alternatively use AnimatedNumber for the Sessions counter and a loading='…' placeholder string for Uptime to visually communicate pending state.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The card-head .card-head has margin-bottom: 16px but the stg-form-fields section has no top padding — fields butt directly against the subtitle with only the card-head margin. The stg-readonly-note at the bottom of the form uses padding: 6px 10px with background recess, creating asymmetric vertical rhythm compared to the stats bar below it.
  - *Fix:* Add padding-top: 4px to .stg-form-fields or a border-top: 1px solid var(--line-1) separator between card-head and fields, consistent with .stg-section-padded used elsewhere in the same page.

**AI Drivers Card (s-ai)** — Vertical list of seven driver rows, each with name + StatusPills (primary, active/inactive, key set) + detail line + default model line + Set Primary button; API-key drivers expand a stg-key-row with password input + Save + Clear; Local LLM driver expands endpoint + model inputs; driverMsg and restart card appear below the list when triggered.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** Seven driver rows render simultaneously with no visual grouping. Subprocess drivers (Claude, Gemini) and API-key drivers (Claude API, Gemini API, OpenAI, Grok) are interleaved with the Local LLM row, which has a completely different UI (two text inputs + Save). The section looks like a flat table even though there are three meaningfully different categories.
  - *Fix:* Add a small section divider or muted fs-xs uppercase label ('Via CLI subscription', 'Via API key', 'Local / self-hosted') above each group using --ink-3 color, matching the muted subgroup labels used in recipe-hub and connector pages. This requires no new primitive — a single <div class='stg-driver-group-label'> with color: var(--ink-3); font-size: var(--fs-xs); margin-bottom: 4px; is sufficient.
- 🔴 **[high/S]** The stg-driver-model line ('Default model: claude-haiku-4-5-20251001') uses --ink-3 at fs-xs — the faintest text on the page. At 11px with ink-3 contrast this likely fails WCAG AA on both themes. It is also factually stale-prone (the comment at line 104 acknowledges this), yet it is rendered on every row as if authoritative.
  - *Fix:* Either remove the default-model line (the comment already says 'authoritative model id is shown on /overview hero') or render it at --ink-2 with a muted 'default:' prefix only on the active/primary row where it is actionable.
- 🟡 **[med/M]** The 'Set primary' button is disabled (opacity 0.45, pointer-events none) for already-primary rows, but the data-active StatusPill shows 'inactive' while isPrimary is true during a pending restart — giving the contradictory appearance of a primary driver that is inactive with no way to act. The stg-restart-card appears only after a successful setPrimary call, not on initial page load if a restart is already pending.
  - *Fix:* On load, if settings?.patchwork?.driver does not match the row whose driverValue equals the server's driver, synthesize the restartPending state from the polled status so the restart card appears immediately. Add aria-live='polite' to the restart card div so screen readers announce the 'Restart Required' state.

**Approval Policy Card (s-approval)** — Three sub-sections: delegation policy select + Save button; time-of-day anomaly checkbox; Claude Code permission rules 3-column grid (allow/ask/deny).

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The delegation policy select (.stg-select) and its Save button sit inline in .stg-gate-row without an explicit label association for the button — the select has id='delegation-policy' but the Save button has only aria-label='Save delegation policy'. The select option text ('off — no gating', 'high — gate high-risk tools', 'all — gate every tool call') front-loads the value key (off/high/all) before the plain-language meaning, which makes the options feel like internal identifiers.
  - *Fix:* Reorder option text to lead with the meaning: 'No gating (off)', 'Gate high-risk tools (high)', 'Gate every tool call (all)'. This follows the 'lead with the signal' copy principle and is a single-line change in the JSX.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The permission rules section falls back to 'No permission data available.' as a plain <p class='stg-help stg-help-mt'> when permRules is null. This covers both the loading state (fetch in-flight) and the error/empty state — users cannot tell if the data hasn't arrived yet or if settings.json has no rules configured.
  - *Fix:* While permRules is null (loading), render three SkeletonList placeholders inside the perm-col grid. Once resolved and empty, use the existing EmptyState primitive (already imported in the page) with a short description: 'No permission rules found in ~/.claude/settings.json'.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The time-of-day anomaly checkbox uses .stg-checkbox-label (a plain flex + label wrapper) while the kill-switch and telemetry sections use the <ToggleRow> component which includes a help-text sub-line and disabled-reason support. The inconsistency means approval-section items look structurally lighter than safety/telemetry items for no functional reason.
  - *Fix:* Migrate the time-of-day anomaly checkbox to use <ToggleRow id='time-of-day-anomaly' label='Time-of-day anomaly signal' help='...' checked={todayAnomaly} onChange={...} />. The existing stg-help-indent error display (todayAnomalyErr) can be passed via a ToggleRow extension or kept adjacent.

**Safety Card — Kill Switch (s-safety)** — card with inline style overrides (borderColor, background) when ksEngaged, containing an emoji ⚠️ in the h2 and a ToggleRow for the kill-switch. The card border and background transition from default to --err tint when engaged.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The engaged state uses inline style={{ borderColor: 'var(--err)', background: 'color-mix(...)' }} — bypassing the token/class system. This means the engaged tint won't adapt correctly if the --card-bg or --surface token is overridden in a custom theme, and it cannot be targeted by CSS for animations or dark/light theme overrides.
  - *Fix:* Add a data-engaged attribute to the card div and move the border/background override to a CSS rule: .card[data-engaged='true'] { border-color: var(--err); background: color-mix(in srgb, var(--err) 4%, var(--card-bg, var(--surface))); }. The transition is already in the inline style and should move there too.
- 🔴 **[high/S]** The ⚠️ emoji in the h2 has aria-hidden='true' but its opacity (0.4 when disengaged, 1 when engaged) creates a visual state change with no accessible equivalent. Screen reader users rely only on the ToggleRow label text ('Kill switch — ENGAGED' vs '... released') which is correct, but the heading text ('Safety') does not change — so AT users scanning headings get no engagement signal.
  - *Fix:* Add an aria-live='polite' wrapping div around the ToggleRow label or add a visually-hidden status span that announces 'kill switch engaged' / 'released' when ksEngaged changes, separate from the emoji opacity treatment.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** When ksLocked is true, the ToggleRow renders with disabled=true and the long disabledReason ('Locked by PATCHWORK_FLAG_KILL_SWITCH_WRITES at bridge startup — restart with that env unset to toggle from here.') appears as .toggle-row-reason in italic fs-xs --ink-3. The text is 90+ characters at the smallest readable font size — likely wraps awkwardly and is styled at opacity faintest tier.
  - *Fix:* Truncate the disabled reason in the ToggleRow to one actionable sentence: 'Locked by env flag — restart bridge without PATCHWORK_FLAG_KILL_SWITCH_WRITES to unlock.' Use --ink-2 (not --ink-3) for the disabled reason text so it meets minimum contrast.

**Mobile / Web Push Card (s-mobile)** — Two sub-sections: push subscription status row (StatusPill) + subscribe/test/unsubscribe actions + halt-notify checkbox; PWA install instructions with inline OS-specific HTML copy.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** When pushStatus is 'loading', only a StatusPill tone='muted' ('Checking…') is shown — the subscribe button is disabled but there is no Skeleton or loading indicator below the status row. The section appears partially empty until the service-worker probe resolves, which can take 200–800ms.
  - *Fix:* Show a skeleton placeholder for the action button area while pushStatus === 'loading': <div className='skeleton' style={{ height: 32, width: 140, borderRadius: 'var(--r-2)' }} />. The Skeleton component is already imported on other pages.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The PWA install instructions (iOS + Android) are plain <p class='stg-help'> with <strong> inline — instructions are long and buried below the action buttons. On mobile viewports the user must scroll past all settings cards to reach install steps, but they most need these instructions BEFORE they can subscribe.
  - *Fix:* When pushStatus === 'unsubscribed' or 'loading', surface a collapsed 'How to install as PWA' disclosure (<details><summary>) immediately above the subscribe button, so the install steps are available before subscription is attempted rather than below it.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The halt-notify checkbox (.stg-push-pref) is only rendered when pushStatus === 'subscribed'. It uses a plain label + checkbox pattern inconsistent with the ToggleRow component used by the telemetry and kill-switch sections.
  - *Fix:* Replace with <ToggleRow id='push-halts-pref' label='Notify when a recipe run halts or errors' help='' checked={haltsPref} onChange={handleHaltsPrefToggle} disabled={haltsPrefBusy} /> for structural consistency. Remove the stg-push-pref class.

**Telemetry Card (s-telemetry)** — Three ToggleRow items (crash reports, usage stats, local diagnostics) + optional meta lines for last-sent-at and endpoint + stg-tel-footer with destructive 'Delete local telemetry data' button.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** All three toggles default to false before the /api/bridge/telemetry-prefs fetch resolves. The toggles are immediately interactive in this false state — a fast user can toggle one before the real server state loads, then the resolved fetch overwrites their change. The telInitialized.current guard prevents re-fetching but does not block optimistic updates during the initial fetch.
  - *Fix:* Disable all three ToggleRows (disabled={!telInitialized.current}) until the initial fetch completes. Show a Skeleton placeholder row for each toggle. This is a single boolean derived from telInitialized.current which can be exposed as a useState.
- 🟡 **[med/M]** The 'Delete local telemetry data' button uses window.confirm() for its destructive confirmation. The globals.css comment at line 8765 notes the button is 27px high (below 32px minimum). The confirm dialog is synchronous, blocks the main thread, and is unstyled — inconsistent with the Dialog primitive used on other destructive actions in the dashboard.
  - *Fix:* Replace window.confirm() with the shared Dialog primitive (already in the codebase) scoped to a short confirmation message. While the dialog is open, show the button in a loading state.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The telEndpoint and telLastSentAt meta lines (stg-tel-meta) appear inside the toggle list gap, visually interleaved with the ToggleRows, making them look like sub-labels of the last toggle rather than section-level metadata.
  - *Fix:* Move the meta lines to a separate div below the toggle list with a border-top: 1px solid var(--line-1) separator, styled at --ink-2 with a 'Reporting to:' / 'Last sent:' label pattern matching the .stg-stats-bar approach in the Bridge card.

**Transient Error Banner** — Single <div class='alert-err'> rendered at the top of the content area when the /status fetch fails ('Unreachable: {err}'); no retry button; no error state for the kill-switch fetch or permission-rules fetch.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The alert-err banner is positioned inside the section tag, above the settings-grid, but the page still renders the full form skeleton below it. The banner says 'Unreachable: {err}' with raw error strings (e.g. '/status 404') that are developer-speak, not user-facing copy.
  - *Fix:* Replace the raw error string with user-facing copy: 'Bridge is unreachable — check that `patchwork start` is running.' Add a Retry button that calls the tick() function immediately. Use the shared ErrorState primitive for consistency when unsupported is true.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** The unsupported EmptyState uses title='Settings endpoint coming in next phase' — this is internal roadmap language shown to end users. The description references patchwork print-token which is a CLI command, not a dashboard action.
  - *Fix:* Change title to 'Bridge version too old' and description to: 'Update Patchwork to a newer version to access settings from this dashboard. Run patchwork print-token in a terminal to check connection details.'

**Loading State (Suspense / RouteLoading)** — layout.tsx is a pass-through; loading.tsx renders <RouteLoading /> via the Next.js Suspense boundary — covers the initial server-side load. Client-side data fetches (settings, permRules, telemetry, push status) have no skeleton states.

- 🔴 **[high/M]** The RouteLoading Suspense boundary covers the page shell but once JS hydrates the page renders fully with empty/default form fields. There are no per-section Skeleton states — all cards appear instantly with empty inputs and '—' placeholders, looking identical to an offline bridge state.
  - *Fix:* Show SkeletonStatCard or a generic card skeleton for the Bridge card while settings is null; show SkeletonList for the driver list and permission columns during their respective fetch windows. The Skeleton primitives are already available and used on other pages.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** There is no loading.tsx or Skeleton guard for the inbox-delivery sub-route (/settings/inbox-delivery/page.tsx exists) — this route has its own layout needs but the parent loading.tsx only covers the settings index.
  - *Fix:* Add a loading.tsx to dashboard/src/app/settings/inbox-delivery/ that returns <RouteLoading /> mirroring the parent, so navigating directly to the sub-route does not flash unstyled content.


### Login  `/login`

**Top 3:**
1. Add role='alert' + aria-live='polite' to the error p in login-form.tsx — screen readers currently silently ignore failed login attempts, a critical accessibility gap on an authentication page.
2. Wrap the form in PatchCard or GlassCard so it sits on --surface with border and radius, establishing visual separation from the raw canvas background that currently makes the form indistinct in both themes.
3. Increase the submit button font-size from --fs-s (12px) to --fs-base (14px) — the primary action on the page is currently rendered smaller than its own label, inverting visual hierarchy.

**Page shell / centering container** — Full-viewport flex column centering a 360px-wide div; background hardcoded to var(--bg-0) via inline style; no card or surface wrapping the form contents.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The form floats directly on the raw canvas color with no surface lift, making the login area visually indistinct from the page background — especially in the light 'paper' theme where --canvas (#f3efe5) and the form inputs bleed together.
  - *Fix:* Wrap the inner div in a PatchCard (or GlassCard with hover=false) so the form sits on --surface with the standard card border, shadow, and radius. This is consistent with how every other content area in the dashboard is surfaced, and both themes support it.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The maxWidth is set twice — 360px on the outer wrapper div and 320px on the form element itself — creating a mismatched constraint that makes the form narrower than its label text region with no benefit.
  - *Fix:* Remove the maxWidth: 320 inline style from the form element in login-form.tsx and let it inherit the 360px from the page wrapper.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** No background pattern, gradient, or any visual anchor exists behind the centered card, so the page feels like an unfinished blank on large screens.
  - *Fix:* Add a subtle radial gradient using --orange-soft or --line-1 at the center of the canvas background for visual depth — consistent with the beam effect used on .card.beam.

**Wordmark / brand header** — An h1 'patchwork' in var(--font-mono) at --fs-xl (16px) with font-weight 700 and 8px bottom margin.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The wordmark is rendered in --font-mono at 16px, which gives it a terminal/code aesthetic but is undersized for a login page focal point — it carries no visual weight and is easy to miss above the subtitle text.
  - *Fix:* Bump the h1 to --fs-2xl (18px) or --fs-3xl (20px), or use --fs-display (28px) with font-weight 600 to establish a clear visual hierarchy between brand, subtitle, and form.
- ⚪ **[low/M]** There is no logo/icon alongside the wordmark — every other dashboard page shows the brand mark in the sidebar. The login page is the first thing users see but has no iconographic anchor.
  - *Fix:* Add the patchwork logomark SVG or a small icon above the h1, consistent with the sidebar brand treatment. Even a simple orange square or icon at 24–32px establishes brand presence.

**Subtitle / instruction text** — A p tag 'Enter the dashboard password to continue.' in --ink-2 at --fs-m (13px) with 24px bottom margin.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The subtitle is purely procedural and adds minimal information value — the form below already has a 'Dashboard password' label and a submit button. The combination of subtitle + label is redundant.
  - *Fix:* Either remove the subtitle and let the label carry the instruction, or shorten the subtitle to something scannable like 'Local access only.' to hint at the security model for users who see this unexpectedly.

**Password input** — A label wrapping an input[type=password] with --recess background, --line-2 border, --r-2 radius, --font-mono font at --fs-m; autoFocus and autoComplete='current-password' set.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The input uses --font-mono for password entry, which is appropriate, but the label text 'Dashboard password' above it is also inheriting the column flex layout font which may mismatch the sans-serif context established by the page. More critically, there is no aria-label or id/htmlFor pairing — the label wraps the input so screen reader association works, but the input has no id for external form targeting.
  - *Fix:* Add an explicit id='password' on the input and a htmlFor='password' on the label element to make the association programmatically robust beyond wrapping.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The input has no focus ring beyond the browser default. Other inputs in the dashboard presumably use a var(--accent) or var(--line-3) outline. The raw browser focus ring can vary across browsers and themes, failing visual consistency.
  - *Fix:* Add a CSS focus-visible rule in globals.css for this input or apply a class that matches the dashboard's standard input focus style (outline: 2px solid var(--accent); outline-offset: 2px).
- ⚪ **[low/S]** When busy=true the input is disabled but there is no loading indicator on or near the input itself — only the button text changes to 'Signing in…'. Users may attempt to re-type during the async wait.
  - *Fix:* Add a subtle spinner (a small rotating CSS border animation) inside or adjacent to the button rather than just changing button text, which is consistent with other loading states in the dashboard.

**Submit button** — A button[type=submit] with var(--accent) background, --on-orange text, --fs-s (12px) font, opacity 0.5 when disabled. Text toggles between 'Sign in' and 'Signing in…'.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The button uses --fs-s (12px) which is below the recommended minimum for interactive button text (14px / --fs-base) and creates a hierarchy where the button is smaller than the label above it — inverting the visual weight of the primary action.
  - *Fix:* Change the button font-size to var(--fs-base) (14px) to make it the clear primary affordance on the page.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The disabled state uses opacity: 0.5 on both busy and empty-password conditions, but these are semantically different states. Busy (loading) should show a spinner or 'Signing in…' with reduced opacity, while empty-password should show a distinct 'nothing typed yet' affordance.
  - *Fix:* Keep opacity: 0.5 for empty-password, but for busy add an aria-busy='true' attribute and a small inline spinner SVG so the state communicates 'working' rather than 'unavailable'.

**Error message display** — A conditional p element in --err color at --fs-s (12px) with margin 0, rendered below the button when err state is non-empty.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The error message has no role='alert' or aria-live='polite' attribute, so screen readers will not announce it when it appears after a failed login attempt.
  - *Fix:* Add role='alert' and aria-live='polite' to the error p element so assistive technology announces the error without requiring focus change.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The 503 error message 'Dashboard auth not configured server-side.' is developer-facing copy that leaks implementation details to end users. A user seeing this message has no actionable path forward.
  - *Fix:* Replace with 'This dashboard is not yet set up. Contact your administrator.' which preserves the signal without exposing server-side config language.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The raw fetch catch block shows JavaScript error messages directly (e.g. 'Failed to fetch', 'NetworkError') with no sanitization for user-facing display.
  - *Fix:* Map common fetch errors to user-friendly messages: check for TypeError (network offline) and show 'Cannot reach the server — check your connection.' instead of the raw JS exception string.


### Global chrome (Shell — on every page)  `(all)`

**Top 3:**
1. Mount the already-built TopBarBreadcrumb component in the Shell header — it is fully implemented but never rendered, leaving every deep page (recipe detail, run detail, session detail) with no top-bar wayfinding context.
2. Change BridgeOfflineBanner's role from 'status' to 'alert' so screen readers interrupt immediately when the bridge goes offline — the current polite announcement means AT users may not hear the banner until after the queue clears.
3. Overhaul the CommandPalette empty state: showing all routes unsorted when the query is blank overwhelms users; curate a short list of recent nav destinations plus live approvals/runs so the palette feels fast and contextual rather than a raw sitemap dump.

**Top bar (app-header)** — Fixed header with hamburger, brand wordmark, command-palette trigger, ActivityTicker, identity pill, theme toggle, bell icon, and avatar link — all crammed into one flex row with no visible dividers.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** TopBarBreadcrumb component is imported from navRoutes but is never rendered inside AppShell — the header has no breadcrumb, so deep pages (e.g. /recipes/foo/edit) show only the brand, giving no location context.
  - *Fix:* Mount <TopBarBreadcrumb /> in the app-header-left between the brand link and the command-palette trigger; it already returns null on root so no extra guard needed.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The topbar-search button reads 'Jump to anything…' in the placeholder AND carries the same text in the CommandPalette input placeholder — duplicated copy with no shortcut affordance visible until the kbd chip appears; on mobile the button label is invisible (hidden via CSS) leaving only an unlabeled search icon.
  - *Fix:* On desktop shorten the visible label to 'Search…' and ensure the .kbd chip '⌘K' is always visible. Add aria-keyshortcuts='Meta+k Control+k' to the button. On mobile ≤768px keep the button but show a compact 14px 'Search' label instead of hiding via topbar-brand-suffix pattern.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** IdentityPill in the header and BridgeStatusBlock in the sidebar footer both show bridge online/offline state simultaneously — two separate status indicators with slightly different wording ('reachable' vs online/offline dot) create visual noise and potential contradiction.
  - *Fix:* Remove the IdentityPill's online/offline dot and host+port text from the top bar on desktop (where the sidebar is always visible). Keep it only for mobile where the sidebar is hidden. On desktop the pill can show just the workspace name without the status dot.

**Sidebar — 'New recipe' CTA button** — An accent-coloured full-width button at the very top of the sidebar, inline-styled with position:relative zIndex:1 and textDecoration:none on a Link.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The inline styles (position, zIndex, textDecoration) duplicate what the sidebar-create class should handle via globals.css — makes the intent opaque and breaks theming when CSS variables are updated.
  - *Fix:* Move position:relative, zIndex:1, textDecoration:none into the .sidebar-create rule in globals.css; remove the inline style props from the JSX.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The button has no aria-label and the icon's aria-hidden is correct, but the visible 'New recipe' text alone is the accessible name — that is fine, but the keyboard focus ring is not visible in the code; confirm .sidebar-create has a :focus-visible outline using --accent with enough contrast against --surface.
  - *Fix:* Add .sidebar-create:focus-visible { outline: 2px solid var(--accent); outline-offset: 2px; } to globals.css if missing.

**Sidebar — nav sections and badges** — Grouped nav links with section labels, icons, active highlight, and three badge types (approvals count, halt count, live-runs count) rendered via navMarkup memo.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The halt-count badge on the Activity nav link caps at 99+ but the More-button badge in MobileBottomNav caps at 9+ — inconsistent overflow display across the same data source.
  - *Fix:* Unify: change the MobileBottomNav badge cap to 99+ to match the sidebar, or extract a shared formatBadgeCount(n, cap=99) util in lib/navRoutes.ts used by both.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** nav-badge for 'runs' gets the class 'is-live' but the halt and approvals badges don't distinguish urgency visually — all three badges look alike despite carrying very different urgency levels (approvals = blocking action, halts = historical, runs = informational).
  - *Fix:* Add is-warn modifier to the halt badge and is-err modifier to the approvals badge in the navMarkup JSX so CSS can style them with --warn and --err respectively, reserving the live pulse animation for run count only.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** app-nav-section-label divs have no role and are not associated with the links beneath them — screen readers cannot distinguish sections.
  - *Fix:* Wrap each section in a <div role='group' aria-label={section.title}> and change the label div to an aria-hidden presentational element, matching the pattern already used in CommandPalette groups.

**Sidebar — BridgeStatusBlock (footer)** — A small two-row block at the bottom of the sidebar showing 'Bridge' label + online/offline dot, then version string + port number.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The version and port are rendered as separate spans with no separator, so 'v0.2.0-beta.12 :3101' reads as one run-on string on narrow sidebars; the port colon prefix ':3101' is unusual notation.
  - *Fix:* Insert an aria-hidden '·' separator between version and port, and display the port as '3101' with a preceding 'port' label or reuse the identity-pill-sep pattern already used in the IdentityPill.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** BridgeStatusBlock carries role='status' and aria-label='Bridge status', but it emits no live update when the status changes — the role='status' implies aria-live='polite' yet the element doesn't re-announce on reconnect.
  - *Fix:* Either add aria-live='polite' explicitly and ensure the status text (not just dot colour) changes on transition, or drop role='status' and make the BridgeOfflineBanner the sole aria-live announcer for offline state.

**Main content area — system banners (BridgeOfflineBanner + KillSwitchBanner)** — Two conditionally-rendered banners injected at the top of <main> before page content: an amber offline banner and a red kill-switch alert; both use fully inline styles with no shared CSS class.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** BridgeOfflineBanner uses role='status' (polite) while KillSwitchBanner uses role='alert' (assertive). The offline banner is the more urgent of the two from a user-action standpoint — the dashboard is non-functional when offline — yet it announces politely, meaning screen readers may queue it behind other announcements.
  - *Fix:* Change BridgeOfflineBanner role to 'alert' (assertive) so it immediately interrupts. KillSwitchBanner is already correct as alert.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** KillSwitchBanner uses fully inline styles with no CSS class, making it impossible to theme via CSS variable overrides and creating a maintenance burden — the var(--fs-xs, var(--fs-s)) fallback pattern indicates the token names are uncertain.
  - *Fix:* Extract .kill-switch-banner and .kill-switch-banner-error classes into globals.css using the --fs-xs and --err tokens directly. Confirm --fs-xs exists in the token set; if not, define it.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The KillSwitchBanner 'Release' button uses the generic .btn class but the locked state only communicates via a title tooltip and a greyed-out (env-locked) span — keyboard and screen-reader users get no accessible description of WHY the button is disabled.
  - *Fix:* Add aria-describedby pointing to a visually hidden span containing the locked reason text when locked=true, so AT reads 'Release — disabled: set by environment variable at startup.'

**GlobalLiveRunsStrip** — Rendered unconditionally in main before page content; component is imported from GlobalLiveRunsStrip but its internal structure is not in the reviewed files.

- 🟡 **[med/S]** The strip is placed between the banners and the page content div (app-content) with no visible separator — when both banners are visible simultaneously with the strip, three distinct chrome elements stack above fold without visual grouping or spacing.
  - *Fix:* Add a margin-bottom: var(--s-2) to .app-content or a border-bottom on GlobalLiveRunsStrip when it has content, ensuring page content starts with a consistent visual rhythm after chrome elements.

**CommandPalette** — Full-screen backdrop with a centered panel, search input, grouped listbox of nav/entity/action results with fuzzy scoring; aria-combobox pattern with aria-activedescendant.

- 🔴 **[high/M]** When the palette opens with no query, ALL commands from ALL groups are shown unsorted — the 'Navigate' group alone surfaces every route, burying entity-level results that are more contextually useful. An empty query state should show a curated 'recent' list, not the entire command index.
  - *Fix:* When query.trim() is empty, show at most the top 3 most-recently-visited nav routes (tracked via sessionStorage) plus any pendingApprovals and active runs — cap the empty state at ~8 rows total so the palette feels fast rather than overwhelming.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** cmdk-row-hint for Approvals group shows a raw callId slice (first 12 chars of a UUID) which is meaningless to users — they need context like 'pending · writeFile' not 'a3f9b2c1d4e5'.
  - *Fix:* Change the Approvals hint to 'pending approval' or show the toolName again with a status prefix, and drop the callId from the visible hint (keep it in id for keying).
- 🟡 **[med/S]** Session results in the palette show a truncated session ID (first 16 chars) as the label — there is no human-readable context. A session ID means nothing to a user scanning results.
  - *Fix:* Use clientType as the primary label (e.g. 'Claude Code session') and the truncated id as the hint, matching the existing hint pattern: label=clientType ?? 'Session', hint=s.id.slice(0,8).

**Mobile bottom navigation (MobileBottomNav)** — Five-tab fixed bottom bar with 4 primary routes and a 'More' overflow button; 'More' opens a sheet dialog with remaining routes displayed as a text-only grid.

- ⚪ **[low/S]** The halt-count badge on the 'More' button uses fully inline styles (no CSS class) including hard-coded px values (top:4, right:calc(50%-16px), height:16, padding:0 4px) — these will break if the icon or button layout changes, and cannot be overridden by theme CSS.
  - *Fix:* Extract a .mobile-more-badge class into globals.css using the nav-badge token values from the sidebar; replace the inline style object with className='mobile-more-badge'.
- ⚪ **[low/M]** The 'More' sheet (mobile-more-sheet-grid) shows route labels as plain text links with no icons — visually inconsistent with the primary tab bar which has icons for every item.
  - *Fix:* Add 16×16 SVG icons to the more-sheet items using the same PATHS constants already defined in Shell.tsx, or at minimum add a small directional arrow (›) to each link to signal navigability.
- 🟡 **[med/S]** The MobileBottomNav aria-label on the <nav> is 'Primary' — this is ambiguous since there is already a sidebar nav with aria-label='Main navigation' on desktop. Screen readers on mobile encounter 'Primary' navigation with no context.
  - *Fix:* Change aria-label to 'Primary navigation' to match the sidebar landmark label, ensuring consistent AT experience across viewport sizes.

**TopBarBreadcrumb** — Client component that builds breadcrumbs from pathname segments using navRoutes map; renders a <nav aria-label='Breadcrumb'> but is never actually mounted in Shell's header JSX.

- 🔴 **[high/S]** The component is fully built and correct but is not used anywhere in Shell.tsx — it is a dead component. The header provides no breadcrumb context, leaving users on deep pages (e.g. /recipes/foo/edit) with no wayfinding in the top bar beyond the sidebar's active highlight.
  - *Fix:* Import and render <TopBarBreadcrumb /> in app-header-left, positioned after the brand link. It already returns null on pathname='/' so the homepage is unaffected.
- ⚪ **[low/S]** Dynamic recipe segments are shown raw (URL-decoded name string) in breadcrumbs — long recipe names will overflow the maxWidth:320 container and truncate silently with text-overflow:ellipsis giving no tooltip.
  - *Fix:* Add title={crumb.label} to both the Link and the span variants so truncated labels reveal on hover, consistent with the ellipsis overflow treatment already in place.
